With great potential for anion detection, the extensive development of CNT-based SC-ISEs provides a wealth of options for a variety of practical ion detection methods, such as in situ aquatic environmental analysis. Since the solid-contact configuration of potentiometric ion sensors has become a new wave due to their unique advantages (e.g., fast response time, reduced size, insensitivity to light and pressure, and no restrictions on the installation angle),60,380,381 the use of CNTs as the ion-to-electron transducers to develop SC-ISEs for the detection of certain ions in water resources is a fairly attractive option.382–385 For instance, Cuartero et al. developed a submersible device containing the control electronics and a replaceable sensing probe module for in situ seawater potentiometric measurements (Fig. 9).382,383 Two kinds of submersible probes consisting of different CNT-based SC-ISEs are respectively designed to detect chloride and macronutrients, or species related to the carbon cycle in seawater. This submersible device can work properly for 3 weeks with the capability of autonomous operation to obtain rapid and trustworthy information.
 Fig. 9  (a) Photographs of the potentiometric flow cell (including the cubic acrylic block flow cell, SC-ISEs, inlet, and outlet). Reproduced with permission.383 Copyright 2017, American Chemical Society. (b) A submersible device for the in situ seawater measurement of pH, salinity, chloride, and nitrate. This submersible device was deployed from a boat with the use of a small onboard crane. Reproduced with permission.382 Copyright 2018, American Chemical Society. 
In view of the excellent conductivity of CNTs, many studies have used CNT-based inks to impart conductivity to some unconventional substrates, which can significantly simplify the electrode structure of SC-ISEs while further expanding their application fields. The group of Andrade demonstrated that SC-ISEs can be produced using conventional filter paper (Fig. 10a),194 cotton yarns,192 or rubbers193 coated with CNTs. In these cases, CNTs serve as both the ion-to-electron transducer and the conductive substrate. Among them, a relatively attractive and widely used assembly protocol is to develop cost-effective paper-based potentiometric ion sensors with the use of conductive CNT paper prepared through directly printing CNT inks onto a conventional filter paper using a paintbrush.194 After coating with the membrane cocktails, the CNT paper-based SC-ISEs can show a similar analytical performance to their counterparts constructed on CNT-coated GC electrodes. Later, they used the CNT paper to develop Li+-ISEs for the detection of the Li+ level in whole blood and serum samples (Fig. 10b).195 However, despite the high hydrophobicity of CNTs, the CNT paper is found to possess a low water contact angle (∼18°) due to the high porosity of untreated filter paper and possible residual surfactants; while the pretreatment of water rinsing can increase its hydrophobicity, its adversely affects the structure.196,314,343 The poor adherence of conductive paper and the possible accumulation of moisture in the pores are also harmful to the performance of these sensors. To this end, Jaworska et al. proposed an alternative simple assembly procedure to obtain disposable potentiometric ion sensors using a tetrahydrofuran (THF) mixture containing MWCNTs and PVC, thereby avoiding the use of surfactants.386 For increasing the hydrophobicity of CNT paper, the group of Chumbimuni-Torres reported a method to fill the pores of the unrinsed CNTs paper by sputtering a layer of gold and then covering with a layer of POT.196 The treated CNT paper exhibits a high contact angle of 116°. Configurated with MMA–DMA enabled ISMs, these CNT paper-based SC-ISEs show nanomolar LODs for K+, Ag+, and Cd2+. They also used a similar approach to prepare paper-strip SC-ISEs for the determination of K+, Na+, and I− levels in body fluids with the use of POT-coated CNT paper.197
 Fig. 10  (a) Photograph of a conductive CNT paper and the SEM image of a filter paper impregnated with a CNT ink. Reproduced with permission.194 Copyright 2012, American Chemical Society. (b) Schematic illustration of the preparation and use of the CNT paper-based potentiometric cell for the measurement of Li+ in the blood sample. Reproduced with permission.195 Copyright 2014, Royal Society of Chemistry. 
Even with these advances, an urgent problem existing for CNT-based SC-ISEs needs to be addressed, namely the insolubility of CNTs in most kinds of solvents with the tendency to self-associate into micro-scale aggregates.387 Regarding obtaining stable homogeneous dispersions of CNTs, the use of surfactants and the functionalization of CNTs are two commonly used methods. Nevertheless, the possible impact of these dispersion methods on sensor performance is a factor that cannot be ignored. The group of Michalska reported an investigation on the effect of surfactants in CNT aqueous solution on the performance of SC-ISEs.314 Three model dispersing agents were evaluated: anionic surfactants (sodium dodecylbenzenesulfonate, DBS), cationic surfactants (cetyltrimetylammoniumchloride, CTAC), and polymeric agents (sodium carboxymethylcellulose, SCMC). When using anionic or cationic surfactants as the dispersing agents, several disadvantages are found, e.g., the reduced hydrophobicity of the solid-contact layer, the risk of surfactant partitioning into the membrane, and the property changes of the CNT layer during the washing procedure. These factors will adversely affect the stability, selectivity, LOD, and lifetime of the sensors. Therefore, the authors suggested the employment of SCMC as the optimized CNT dispersing agent to minimize the effects of surfactants. However, it is also found that excessive use of SCMC as the dispersing agent in CNT solution, especially for the preparation of CNT paper, may result in a large amount of interfering Na+ ions at the back side of the ISM, thereby affecting the potentiometric performance of SC-ISEs.152 In other cases, the lipophilic functionalization of CNTs with octadecylamine (ODA) makes them conveniently soluble in organic solvents, which seems to be more popular due to the complete avoidance of surfactants and aqueous solutions.146,177,183,289,384,388 In addition to the issue about the dispersion of CNTs, the purification of CNTs before their further use should also be considered, as CNTs always contain metal oxide catalyst residues and amorphous carbon particles.208 During the purification process using high temperature or strong acid, however, a common but undesirable phenomenon is the increase of pH sensing groups (such as carboxyl groups) on the surfaces of CNTs, which will reduce the anti-interference ability of CNT-based SC-ISEs.
In order to obtain efficient solid-contact layers, efforts have also been made to develop CNT-based nanocomposites for use as ion-to-electron transducers. When other materials are incorporated, the processability of CNTs in solution allows the production of new composite materials that are also attractive options as solid-contact layers due to their possible superior properties. For example, the group of Bobacka found that the combination of carboxylated MWCNTs with PEDOT is beneficial to the redox behavior, as confirmed by CV and EIS characterization.199,389 Liu et al. demonstrated that the incorporation of bimetallic AuCu nanoparticles into MWCNTs (AuCuNPs–MWCNTs) is beneficial for facilitating the charge transfer and increasing the double-layer capacitance.201 The group of Michalska introduced the cobalt(II) porphyrin/cobalt(III) corrole pair onto the surface of MWCNTs (Ph(Co2+)/Cor(Co2+)–MWCNTs) to obtain an improved ion-to-electron transducer.252 The advantages of this type of SC-ISE are high E0 reproducibility (±0.7 mV, n = 4) and low LOD (10−8.3 M for K+). Besides, they synthesized a composite material consisting of MWCNTs and POT (MWCNTs–POT) as the enhanced transducer for SC-ISEs.200 The POT is used as a dispersing agent for MWCNTs and can immobilize on MWCNTs, thereby avoiding the use of surfactants and preventing the spontaneous unwanted partition of POT into the membrane phase. Furthermore, the MWCNTs–POT film shows a higher hydrophobicity, conductivity, and capacitance than the POT film. The SC-ISEs constructed using MWCNTs–POT possess an improved potential stability and the E0 reproducibility between six electrodes in one batch is less than 3 mV.


3.2.4 Carbon nanohorns. 
Single-walled carbon nanohorns (SWCNHs) have a structure similar to SWCNTs. They are GR-based horn-shaped sheaths and possess fine intrinsic properties, such as high specific surface area and electrical conductivity.390,391 Based on these interesting properties, our group has evaluated the potentiometric performance of SWCNH-based Ca2+-ISEs and REs.202 The electron transfer kinetics were detailedly studied by the EIS measurement, demonstrating the beneficial effects of the SWCNH-based solid-contact layer. Compared with CWEs, the introduction of the SWCNH layer as the ion-to-electron transducer significantly improves the potential stability of SC-ISEs as a result of a larger double-layer capacitance. In addition, the SWCNH-based REs also exhibit good potential stability for common ions with different charges over a wide concentration range.


3.2.5 Graphene. 
Since first exfoliated from graphite in 2004,392 GR has become a superstar in the field of materials science.393–397 As a member of 2D carbon nanomaterials, GR possesses the prominent properties of large surface area, high electron transfer capability, stable chemical properties, and excellent hydrophobicity owing to its unique one-atom-thick sp2-hybridized carbon sheet structure,398,399 which is thus an attractive and promising solid-contact functional material for SC-ISEs. In 2011, our group proposed the use of chemically reduced GR oxide (CRGO) as the ion-to-electron transducer for SC-ISEs.203 The CRGO-based K+-ISEs exhibit satisfactory potentiometric performance, including good long-term potential stability (12.6 µV h−1), fast response (less than 10 s), and excellent interference immunity to O2, CO2, light, and redox couples. The results of EIS characterization show that the presence of the CRGO layer is beneficial for reducing interfacial resistance and accelerating charge transfer. The double-layer capacitance of the CRGO-based K+-ISEs obtained from the CRC measurement is about 78.1 µF. The group of Rius further conducted detailed research on the transduction mechanism of the solid-contact layer, and the results suggest that the CRGO film can act as an asymmetric capacitor.204
The commonly used approach for the preparation of CRGO is based on chemical oxidation and reduction and then using a multi-step drip-coating method to prepare the CRGO-based solid-contact layer.204,206,207 Nevertheless, the chemical redox process of CRGO may involve toxic reducing agents, and the cumbersome modification step for the CRGO layer is obviously not conducive to its practical application. To this end, our group proposed an alternative method for the preparation of the GR-based solid-contact layer to replace the conventional multi-step drop-casting method, which is termed the one-step electrodeposition technique.208 In this way, GR oxide (GO) can be directly reduced on a screen-printed electrode to form an electrochemically reduced GO (ERGO) layer, showing the advantages of efficiency and reproducibility. Using this method, we developed a disposable potentiometric ion strip containing a pair of ERGO-based SC-ISE and RE for the determination of Ca2+ levels in milk and water.400 The analysis results obtained from this device are comparable to the standard atomic absorption spectrometry (AAS) method. Another effective method to avoid toxic agents and simplify the assembly procedure is the use of laser-induced GR (LIG) as the solid-contact layer for SC-ISEs. In recent years, LIG has attracted extensive research interest, which can be directly generated on a variety of solid substrates using a one-step laser-assisted processing technique.401,402 With this simple, rapid, and chemical-free fabrication method, Garland and coworkers prepared flexible LIG electrodes on polyimide (PI) films and functionalized these electrodes with NO3−-ISM or NH4+-ISM to measure nitrogen levels in soil slurries (Fig. 11a).210 These LIG-based SC-ISEs exhibit comparable performance to commercial electrodes in the soil slurry recovery test, with a recovery percentage of ∼95%.
 Fig. 11  (a) LIG-based SC-ISEs for the measurement of nitrogen levels in the soil sample. Reproduced with permission.210 Copyright 2018, American Chemical Society. (b) Photographs of GNP and the preparation of flexible GNP-based SC-ISEs. Reproduced with permission.212 Copyright 2019, American Society of Agricultural and Biological Engineers. (c) The fabrication and performance of a GR-based K+-ISE. Reproduced with permission.213 Copyright 2017, American Chemical Society. (d) The preparation of a GR ink-based all-written potentiometric ion sensor. Reproduced with permission.214 Copyright 2018, American Chemical Society. 
In order to simplify the electrode structure of GR-based SC-ISEs, an attractive approach is to utilize the unique properties (e.g., excellent conductivity and the self-assembling feature) of GR to make it both an effective ion-to-electron transducer and a flexible conductive substrate.403,404 Taking the free-standing GR paper (GNP) as an example, this material possesses excellent mechanical robustness, structural uniformity, and good hydrophobicity and electrical conductivity.405,406 Our group reported a flexible planar potentiometric sensing device based on a flexible GNP substrate.211 Three types of GNP-based SC-ISEs were constructed to detect H+, K+, and Ca2+. Combined with GNP-based SC-REs, this device possesses a comparable performance to conventional potentiometric detection systems. The high hydrophobicity (contact angle 103.7°) of GNP ensures that no water layer is formed underneath the sensing membrane. Later, we also reported a GNP-based SC-ISE for the determination of Pb2+ in water samples (Fig. 11b).212 The long-term stability test shows that these Pb2+-ISEs can maintain their initial sensitivity of 98.5% after 15 days of storage.
Apart from the self-assembly strategies, the coating of GR-based inks on some nonconductive substrates to construct SC-ISEs is another promising approach to simplify the electrode structure of GR-based SC-ISEs. For instance, the group of Claussen proposed a manufacturing method for SC-ISEs using the inkjet-printed technique to fabricate GR electrodes (Fig. 11c).213 The GR electrode was processed through a post-print annealing process in a nitrogen ambient environment after being printed on a silicon wafer, which can increase the electrical conductivity of the GR electrode and make its surface more porous. The resulting SC-ISEs can detect K+ in a complex artificial eccrine perspiration solution with good selectivity. However, the need for a high-temperature process complicates their fabrication and limits the choice of electrode substrate. Later, our group reported a flexible all-written potentiometric ion sensor based on a highly conductive GR ink, which does not require thermal treatment after preparation (Fig. 11d).214 A Chinese brush-based writing technique was used to prepare a pair of GR ink-based SC-ISE and SC-RE on a PET substrate. The resulting Cd2+-ISEs exhibit a better analytical performance than their GC-based or graphite ink-based counterparts. In addition, An et al. used a spray technique to construct GR electrodes on a chromatography paper and found that the prepared GR layer appears to be wrinkled with a high surface roughness, ensuring a large contact area with the sensing membrane.215 Based on these GR electrodes, they developed a multichannel wearable potentiometric ion-sensing device for real-time monitoring of multiple ions in sweat.
The increase in the effective contact area between the solid-contact layer and the sensing membrane is a well-known approach to obtain higher double-layer capacitance. In this regard, some GR materials with 3D structures have received attention due to their large specific surface area. The group of Qin utilized a 3D GR sponge (3D GRS) to develop a freestanding solid-contact Cu2+-ISE (Fig. 12a).217 This material possesses a well-defined cross-linked 3D interconnected porous structure that can provide more sites for ion diffusion and adsorption, thereby facilitating ion-to-electron transfer. A large double-layer capacitance of approximately 500 µF is confirmed by the CRC measurement. The obtained 3D GRS-based SC-ISEs exhibit stable potential response with a low LOD (2.5 × 10−9 M). Yoon and coworkers synthesized a 3D CRGO hydrogel with a porous structure and a large surface area through a hydrothermal self-assembly method (Fig. 12b).218 In this 3D structure, the CRGO nanosheets interconnect with each other and appear to be exfoliated and wrinkled, without obvious aggregation. For the preparation of a CRGO hydrogel-based solid-contact layer, a piece of CRGO hydrogel was first sonicated in 1-methyl-2-pyrrolidinone (NMP) and then dropped onto the surface of the Au electrode. Compared with CWEs, the potential drift of CRGO hydrogel-based SC-ISEs is significantly reduced as a result of increased double-layer capacitance. Furthermore, they also fabricated a potentiometric ion sensing device integrated with an Arduino-based printed circuit board (PCB) for wireless detection of K+ levels in various beverages.
 Fig. 12  (a) Photograph of 3D GRS-based SC-ISEs and the SEM image of 3D GRS. Reproduced with permission.217 Copyright 2019, Elsevier. (b) Photograph of a CRGO hydrogel and the SEM image of CRGO. The flexible CRGO hydrogel-based potentiometric K+ sensor can work normally in a bent state. Reproduced with permission.218 Copyright 2020, Springer Nature. (c) SEM images of defect-free GR and cross-sectional view of defect-free GR layers and ISM layers on PET substrates. Reproduced with permission.209 Copyright 2020, Elsevier. (d) TEM image of tGR nanosheets. Reproduced with permission.220 Copyright 2020, Elsevier. (e) SEM image of the GR–AgTFPB composite. Reproduced with permission.221 Copyright 2015, Elsevier. (f) SEM image of the PtNPs–pGR composite. Reproduced with permission.236 Copyright 2017, Elsevier. (g) SEM image of the Fe3O4–CRGO composite. Reproduced with permission.223 Copyright 2017, Elsevier. 
Even with these advances, it is worth noting that the residual hydrophilic functional groups after the incomplete reduction of GO may adversely affect the long-term stability of the sensors. For example, the group of Niu applied CRGO nanosheets in K+-ISEs as the solid-contact layer.205 It is found that a large amount of residual carboxylic groups on the CRGO nanosheet surface may reduce the inhibitory effect on the formation of a water layer.407 The group of Michalska reported a comparative study of the performance of carboxylated GR (cGR) and CPs (PEDOT, PANI, and POT) as the solid-contact layers.219 They found that the cGR-based solid-contact layer is similar to the PANI-based one in some respects due to the presence of pH-sensitive surface functional groups. In order to avoid these possible negative effects, Park et al. prepared defect-free GR nanosheets by a fluid-dynamic shear exfoliation process, which are characterized by their high-quality crystalline structure without basal plane defects (Fig. 12c).209 The screen-printing technique was used to fabricate K+-ISEs using the defect-free GR-based solid-contact layer. The obtained SC-ISEs exhibit excellent interference immunity. In addition, some work has reported the use of functionalized GR as the solid-contact layer. For instance, Liu et al. used thiol-functionalized GR (tGR) as the ion-to-electron transducer for SC-ISEs, which can self-assemble at the surface of the Au electrode through covalent linkage to form a stable solid-contact layer (Fig. 12d).220 Two kinds of tGR-based SC-ISEs were developed for the determination of K+ and NO3− in continuous flowing sample solutions, exhibiting good analytical performance over 2 weeks.
Similar to CNTs, GR can also be used to incorporate with other materials to synthesize nanocomposites with enhanced ion-to-electron ability. For example, Sun et al. synthesized a GR–AgTFPB nanocomposite as the ion-to-electron transducer for K+-ISEs (Fig. 12e).221 The doped AgTFPB can fix the phase boundary potential via a reversible redox reaction that occurred at the interface between the solid-contact layer and the underlying Ag electrode, thus improving the E0 reproducibility of SC-ISEs between electrodes. The group of Paczosa-Bator introduced two kinds of redox couples (TTF253 and TCNQ258) into GR-based solid-contact layers to prepare hybrid redox and double-layer capacitance transducers, which are proved to improve the potential stability and reproducibility of SC-ISEs. Boeva and Lindfors used a GR and PANI nanocomposite (GR–PANI) as the ion-to-electron transducer to develop SC-ISEs.222 Configurated with SR-based ISMs, the prepared GR–PANI-based Ca2+-ISEs show a low LOD of 5 × 10−8 M. The E0 reproducibility between electrodes is also improved (±4 mV, n = 3) compared to the PANI-based ones. The group of Qin introduced PtNPs into porous GR (PtNPs–pGR) as the solid-contact layer for SC-ISEs (Fig. 12f).236 The presence of PtNPs on the surface of GR leads to the formation of cross-linking sites and therefore protects GR from irreversible aggregation and restacking, maintaining its advantage of large surface area. This improvement results in a significant increase in double-layer capacitance (625 µF). The prepared Cd2+-ISEs based on PtNPs–pGR exhibit a low LOD of 10−8.8 M with an E0 reproducibility (SD) of ±2.5 mV (n = 3). In addition, some GR-based nanocomposites also exhibit interesting physical properties. For example, the group of Qin proposed a magnetic field-directed self-assembly strategy for preparing the solid-contact layer with the use of Fe3O4–CRGO magnetic powder (Fig. 12g).223 The magnetic powder can be physically adsorbed on the surface of the Au electrode under the magnetic field without any liquid dispersants. The resulting Fe3O4–CRGO magnetic powder-based Ca2+-ISEs show a comparable potentiometric performance to other GR-based counterparts and reliable performance in the detection test of Ca2+ levels in artificial seawater.


3.2.6 Carbon black. 
CB is a very fluffy and fine powder form of amorphous carbon with large surface area, high hydrophobicity, and stable chemical properties.408,409 Paczosa-Bator demonstrated that CB can be used as the ion-to-electron transducer in SC-ISEs.410 These CB-based SC-ISEs exhibit a typical Nernstian response toward K+ and good resistance to gas and light interferences. The same group also investigated the effects of different types of nanosized CBs as solid-contact layers and found that the higher specific surface area and larger particle size of CB are more beneficial for improving the potential stability and reproducibility of SC-ISEs.224 Based on the CB-based solid-contact layer, they also constructed a potentiometric multi-sensor platform by combining different SC-ISEs and a RE in an epoxy resin body for the determination of K+, Na+, Cl−, and NO3− in different water samples.411 With the use of CB ink coated cotton threads, Mousavi et al. proposed a miniaturized SC-ISE array (Fig. 13a).225 Through coating different ISM cocktails on conductive threads, four types of thread-based SC-ISEs were fabricated for the detection of K+, Na+, Ca2+, and Cl−, respectively. These miniaturized SC-ISEs can be easily bundled together to develop a multiplexed ion-sensing platform, which can perform ion analysis in different complex matrixes with a small sample volume (200 µL). Moreover, by optimizing the CB ink, the miniaturized K+-ISEs are reported to achieve an E0 reproducibility between electrodes of ±2.3 mV (SD).
 Fig. 13  (a) An SC-ISE array based on a CB ink coated cotton thread for multiple ion analysis. The CB ink and membrane cocktail were deposited on the cotton thread successively for the construction of SC-ISEs. Reproduced with permission.225 Copyright 2018, Royal Society of Chemistry. (b) SEM image of the individual particles of C60-enriched CB. Reproduced with permission.227 Copyright 2013, Elsevier. (c–e) SEM images of CB (c), CB–GR–FP composite (d), and cross-sectional view of a PVC-based ISM coated CB–FP layer (e). Reproduced with permission.226 Copyright 2015, Elsevier. 
In addition, CB is usually used as a composite component in different solid-contact functional materials to increase the contact area of the SC|ISM interface and ensure high electronic conductivity, hydrophobicity, and capacitance of the solid-contact layer.133,227,262 For example, the group of Mikhelson evaluated the effects of the component ratio of the solid-contact layer containing C60-enriched CB, a poly(amidoacid) Cu(I) complex, and an electron–ion exchange resin EI-21 on the potentiometric performance of SC-ISEs (Fig. 13b).227 A rather high contact angle of 180° is obtained when the solid-contact layer contains C60-enriched CB. In the best case, the prepared K+-ISEs exhibit excellent long-term potential stability (3.3 mV over 80 days). The group of Paczosa-Bator demonstrated that SC-ISEs based on CB modified with PtNPs possess a better long-term potential stability and reproducibility than the counterparts based on a single component.233,234 They also prepared a solid-contact layer containing the nanocomposites of carbon materials (CB and GR) and a fluoropolymer (FP), which became superhydrophobic (contact angle >150°) after additional thermal treatment (Fig. 13c–e).226 In another study, it was proved that CB mixed with various molecular organic materials (TTF and TCNQ) can be used as effective ion-to-electron transducers for SC-ISEs to facilitate charge transfer and improve potential stability.254

3.3 Metal nanomaterials
In the last decade, the use of metal nanomaterials as the solid-contact layers for SC-ISEs has received increasing attention due to their high conductivity and large surface-to-volume ratio. Except for the commonly-used drop-casting method, metal nanomaterials can also be readily electrodeposited onto conductive metal substrates to prepare the solid-contact layers. Based on these advantages, metal nanomaterials have become promising candidates for use in SC-ISEs as the ion-to-electron transducers.

3.3.1 Gold nanomaterials. 
The introduction of gold nanomaterials with large surface area on the surface of commonly used conductive metal substrates by electrochemical methods has proven to be a simple and effective approach to increase the double-layer capacitance. For example, the group of Qin used a multicyclic electrochemical alloying/dealloying method to directly generate the nanoporous gold (NPAu) film on the surface of the gold wire electrode as the solid-contact layer for SC-ISEs (Fig. 14a).228 Miniaturized NPAu-based K+-ISEs were fabricated by covering the NPAu film with the membrane cocktail. Benefitting from the increased contact area with the sensing membrane, these miniaturized SC-ISEs exhibit a lager double-layer capacitance than the same-sized CWEs, thus leading to improved potential stability. It was also demonstrated that the NPAu film coated electrode was reusable after removing the failed ISM with organic solvents. In addition, there is another simpler method, called the one-step electrodeposition technique, for in situ preparation of a variety of gold nanostructures on conductive metal substrates. For instance, Wang and coworkers used this electrodeposition method to prepare gold nanodendrite (AuND)-based solid-contact layers on the surface of the micro-Au electrode for the fabrication of planar Na+-ISEs (Fig. 14b).229 The real surface area of the AuND layer is calculated by integrating the adsorption charge of the reduction peak of the CV curve. When the surface area is 7.23 cm2, a low potential drift of about 0.04 mV s−1 is obtained. These AuND-based SC-ISEs can maintain a relatively stable and repeatable calibration curve for at least two months. In combination with SC-ISEs and SC-REs, a wearable sweatband sensor platform was built to real-time monitor Na+ levels in sweat during indoor cycling. Hussien and Derar prepared a layer of 3D spongy-like nanoporous gold (sNPAu) film on the surface of the Pt electrode by direct electrochemical deposition and used it to develop an sNPAu-based SC-ISE for the detection of memantine (a pharmaceutical compound) with an LOD of 2.5 × 10−6 M (Fig. 14c).230
 Fig. 14  (a) SEM image of an NPAu film. Reproduced with permission.228 Copyright 2014, American Chemical Society. (b) SEM images of an AuND array prepared by electrodeposition at different deposition times. Reproduced with permission.229 Copyright 2017, American Chemical Society. (c) SEM image of an sNPAu film. Reproduced with permission.230 Copyright 2019, Springer Nature. (d) TEM image of AuNCs. Reproduced with permission.145 Copyright 2016, Elsevier. 
Other gold nanomaterials, such as gold nanoparticles (AuNPs) and AuNCs, can also be used as ion-to-electron transducers. In 2011, Jaworska and coworkers verified the possibility of AuNPs to be used as ion-to-electron transducers for SC-ISEs.231 Before drop-casting on the surface of the GC electrode, the AuNPs were modified with aliphatic thiols (e.g., octanethiol or butylthiol) to offer enhanced lipophilicity. As a comparison, the long-term stability of AuNP-based SC-ISEs is better than the POT-based ones. Later, the same group utilized dithizone modified AuNPs (AuNPs@Dit) as the solid-contact layer to develop Cu2+-ISEs.154 The AuNPs@Dit-based solid-contact layer can selectively bind to Cu2+ underneath the ISM, thus affecting the ion-fluxes at the SC|ISM interface with the generation of super-Nernstian response. When the solid-contact layer was preloaded with Cu2+ (AuNPs@Dit–Cu) through conditioning in CuSO4 solution, this phenomenon disappeared and a low LOD (3.16 × 10−8 M) was obtained. Following this work, the group of Diamond further investigated the impact of the functional ligands of AuNPs on the performance characteristics of the SC-ISEs.412 Through comparing two different solid-contact layers based on lipoic acid- or lipoic amide-modified AuNPs, they found the adjustability of the potentiometric performance of SC-ISEs with the use of different functionalized AuNPs as solid-contact layers and pointed out the importance of matching the functional ligands to the primary ion.
The use of an anion doped AuNC film as the ion-to-electron transducing layer was proposed by the group of Niu.144 This functional material is a redox couple with equimolar mixed valence, which is prepared by doping arenethiolate monolayer-protected AuNCs with tetrakis(4-chlorophenyl)borate (AuNCs–TB) using a two-phase method. Its well-defined ion exchange function is conducive to the stability of the phase boundary potential at the SC|ISM interface. The AuNCs–TB film also possesses some excellent properties, such as high chemical stability, electrical conductivity, and hydrophobicity. The AuNCs–TB film enabled K+-ISEs to show low potential drift (10.1 ± 0.3 µV h−1 over 72 h) with good interference immunity. Their response characteristics and standard potential E0 are reported to change little during the first 6 weeks. In order to reduce synthesis time and increase yield, the same group used a more efficient synthesis method (namely the one-phase method) to prepare AuNCs@TB and again verified its feasibility as the solid-contact layer for K+-ISEs (Fig. 14d).145 The relationship between performance characteristics and storage time was further studied, and the results show that the LOD is reduced from the original 1.55 × 10−7 M to 1.91 × 10−5 M after one year of storage in KCl solution due to the partial dissolution of AuNCs@TB into the membrane and the leakage of membrane components. In addition, hexanethiolate monolayer-protected AuNCs were used as the ion-to-electron transducers in the PVC matrix of the ISM to prepare K+-ISEs.413 This approach has been proved to improve the potential stability and lifespan without affecting the potentiometric characteristics.


3.3.2 Platinum nanomaterials. 
In 2012, Paczosa-Bator et al. studied the performance of solid-contact K+-ISEs using PtNPs as ion-to-electron transducers (Fig. 15a).232 In view of the large surface-to-volume ratio of PtNPs, these PtNP-based K+-ISEs possess a large double-layer capacitance compared to CWEs, thus exhibiting better potential stability. Interestingly, when PtNPs are used as the solid-contact layer, SC-ISEs do not show significant gas sensitivity compared to the ISEs that use PtNPs as the membrane additive.414 In order to enhance the ion-to-electron transduction ability of PtNP-based solid-contact transducers, PtNPs are commonly hybridized with other functional materials, such as CB233,234 and GR.235,236 For example, Paczosa-Bator et al. demonstrated the use of PtNP modified CB (PtNPs–CB) as the solid-contact layer for SC-ISEs and found that this hybrid transducer can significantly reduce the membrane resistance and improve the potentiometric performance (Fig. 15b).233 These PtNPs–CB nanocomposite-based K+-ISEs and NO3−-ISEs exhibit excellent long-term potential stability (8.2 ± 1.4 µV h−1 and 6.3 ± 1.2 µV h−1 over 172 h, respectively) and high E0 reproducibility between electrodes (±1.4 mV and ±0.2 mV, n = 5, after 72 h of conditioning, respectively).
 Fig. 15  (a) TEM image of PtNPs (inset: SAED pattern recorded from PtNPs). Reproduced with permission.232 Copyright 2012, Royal Society of Chemistry. (b) SEM image of the PtNPs–CB composite. Reproduced with permission.233 Copyright 2013, American Chemical Society. (c) SEM image of Pt nanopetals (left). Photograph of a microfabricated device containing Pt nanopetal-based SC-ISEs (inset: the sensor chamber for continuous monitoring of K+) (right). Reproduced with permission.238 Copyright 2016, Royal Society of Chemistry. (d) SEM images of Pt nanoflowers (left). Cross-sectional view of Pt/Pt nanoflowers/Li+-ISM (right). Reproduced with permission.239 Copyright 2018, Elsevier. (e) SEM images of AgNPs (left) and the Ag@AgCl nanocomposite (right). Reproduced with permission.240 Copyright 2020, Elsevier. 
For the purpose of avoiding the drop-casting step, the electrodeposition technique is always used to prepare Pt nanomaterial-based solid-contact transducers. For example, Taurino et al. electrosynthesized Pt nanopetals or nanospheres on Pt electrodes for the fabrication of SC-ISEs.237 These solid-contact K+-ISEs based on Pt nanopetals or nanospheres exhibit a reduced potential drift and total electrode resistance compared to their counterparts constructed on the bare Pt electrodes. Later, they constructed an acute potentiometric device using Pt nanopetal-based K+-ISEs for monitoring cell death (Fig. 15c).238 Criscuolo et al. fabricated solid-contact Li+-ISEs using Pt nanoflowers as the solid-contact layer (Fig. 15d).239 The large contact area of the SC|ISM interface was observed in the scanning electron microscope (SEM) cross-sectional view. They compared the performances of SC-ISEs based on different solid-contact layers (Pt nanoflowers or Au nanocorals) and conductive substrates (Au or Pt) and found that the combination of the Pt/Pt nanoflowers/Li+-ISM performed the best in terms of potential stability and reproducibility.415 Besides, they also used this method to construct miniaturized Pt nanoflower-based Li+-ISEs which showed a similar potentiometric performance to their macro-counterparts.416


3.3.3 Silver nanomaterials. 
The conventional Ag/AgCl reference system is commonly used and effective for liquid-contact ISEs. For the pursuit of a similar function, the group of Qin utilized AgNPs to develop an inorganic redox buffer of Ag@AgCl/1-tetradecyl-3-methylimidazolium chloride (TMMCl) as the ion-to-electron transducer for SC-ISEs (Fig. 15e).240 The free Cl− is offered by TMMCl. The prepared solid-contact Ca2+-ISEs are insensitive to O2, CO2, and light and can maintain a relatively stable potential response for one month.

3.4 Metal oxide macro/nanomaterials
About a dozen years ago, SnO2/ITO glass417,418 and AgI–Ag2O–V2O5 glass419 were ever used as ion-to-electron transducers to develop SC-ISEs, but the limited potential reproducibility and the possible formation of a water layer restricted their further applications due to the non-ideal homogeneity of the glass layer. In recent years, due to the continuous emergence of a variety of metal oxide macro/nanomaterials, they have begun to be used as ion-to-electron transducers for SC-ISEs and have shown certain potential as alternatives to carbon and noble metal nanomaterials.
The implementation of metal oxide macro/nanomaterials as solid-contact layers to realize the ion-to-electron transduction function mainly relies on two strategies: high specific surface area and high redox activity. The earlier metal oxide macro/nanomaterials used in SC-ISEs as ion-to-electron transducers are some nanostructured ZnO and CuO materials. Khun and coworkers constructed Sr2+-ISEs based on ZnO nanorods that were synthesized on the gold-coated glass substrate by a hydrothermal growth method (Fig. 16a).241 They also developed ZnO nanotube-based I−-ISEs.242 The hollow structures of ZnO nanotubes can provide a larger surface area than ZnO nanorods. In addition, the CuO nanoflower-based Cd2+-ISEs exhibit a LOD at the nanomolar level (Fig. 16b).243 In other studies, the group of Qin evaluated the feasibility of MoO2 microspheres as ion-to-electron transducers (Fig. 16c), which were synthesized from MoO3 nanobelts and dissolved in the THF solvent.244 Compared to the CWEs, the introduction of MoO2 microspheres improves the performance of SC-ISEs to some extent as a result of the enhanced double-layer capacitance. Yang et al. fabricated solid-contact K+-ISEs based on 2D MnO2 nanosheets for the determination of K+ in the blood (Fig. 16d).245 The MnO2 nanosheets have a wrinkled morphology, thereby preventing their dense accumulation and maintaining the advantage of high surface area, which is advantageous for achieving a large double-layer capacitance. Furthermore, Zhao et al. demonstrated that the incorporation of graphdiyne oxide (GDYO) into a MnO2-based solid-contact layer can enhance the potential stability of SC-ISEs and help to inhibit the formation of a water layer.246
 Fig. 16  (a) SEM image of ZnO nanorods. Reproduced with permission.241 Copyright 2013, Elsevier. (b) SEM image of CuO nanoflowers. Reproduced with permission.243 Copyright 2013, Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH & Co. KGaA, Weinheim. (c) SEM image of MoO2 microspheres. Reproduced with permission.244 Copyright 2017, Elsevier. (d) SEM image of MnO2 nanosheets. Reproduced with permission.245 Copyright 2019, Chinese Journal of Analytical Chemistry. (e) SEM image of RuO2 nanoparticles. (f) SEM image of the RuO2–POT composite. Reproduced with permission.249 Copyright 2019, Elsevier. 
Some metal oxide nanomaterials with excellent redox properties can also be used as ion-to-electron transducers. For example, the group of Paczosa-Bator introduced RuO2 nanoparticles into solid-contact H+- and K+-ISEs as ion-to-electron transducers.247,248 The RuO2 nanoparticles are dissolved in dimethylformamide (DMF) solution and drop-cast onto the surface of the GC electrode to prepare the solid-contact layer. Remarkably, these RuO2 nanoparticle-based SC-ISEs exhibit a large redox capacitance at the millifarad level. The same group also prepared a composite material containing RuO2 nanoparticles and POT (RuO2–POT) (Fig. 16e and f).249 This composite exhibits superhydrophobic properties (contact angle 149°). The results of CRC demonstrate that these SC-ISEs possess a rather large capacitance of approximately 3 mF, which is much larger than that of the POT-based ones. Compared to the counterparts based on the single component, RuO2–POT composite-based K+-ISEs exhibit a shorter equilibration time and better potential stability and reproducibility.
3.5 Molecular redox couples
A well-defined redox buffer on the back side of the ISM has long been considered to be an effective approach to improve the potential stability and reproducibility of SC-ISEs. For an adequate redox buffer, its redox potential should be clearly defined and constant, which is also one of the reasons why CPs are not ideal redox buffers. The electric potential (E′) of a redox buffer is determined by the oxidized and reduced species of the redox couple, as predicted by the Nernst equation:136,257,420 (7)where n is the number of electron moles transferred in the redox reaction, E0′ is the standard reduction potential of the redox couple, and aox and ared represent the activities of the oxidized and reduced species of the redox couple, respectively. Ideally, for a redox buffer-based SC-ISE, when the concentration of primary ions in the sample solution is 1 M and thus each phase boundary potential is constant, the EMF of the whole galvanic cell only depends on the E′ of redox buffer.140 Therefore, a well-controlled concentration ratio of the reduced and oxidized species of the redox couple is essential to achieve high E0 reproducibility for this type of SC-ISE. Generally, this concentration ratio is expected to be equal, enabling the interference immunity of the redox buffer towards the redox-active impurities in the system and the polarization effects caused by current during the measurement. Furthermore, these redox couples should possess stable chemical properties with reversible redox activity and rapid ion exchange properties to enable the function of ion-to-electron transfer of the redox buffer-enabled transducer.
The approach of using a redox couple in SC-ISEs can be performed in different ways. The incorporation of a redox couple into the ISM that is directly connected to a conductive substrate can be considered as a simplified idea instead of acting as the solid-contact layer separately,421,422 while the solid-contact layer based on the functional material doped with a redox couple is expected to provide enhanced benefits for ion-to-electron transfer. In earlier studies, considerable efforts have been devoted to using a variety of redox couples to promote charge transfer and stabilize the interfacial potential. For example, lipophilic Ag+ ionophore complexes present in the ISM can stabilize the interface potential via reversible redox reaction with the silver epoxy substrate.423,424 However, in terms of the selectivity of the ISM, this method may not be an appropriate choice when used with other ionophores. Besides, silver tetraphenylborate (AgTPB) was commonly used to construct SC-ISEs.19 In the configuration of Ag/AgTPB/ISM (TPB− as the additive), the phase boundary potential can be well defined. Although the finite lipophilicity and the light sensitivity of this material limit its further application,425 this approach has good heuristic value as an early attempt.144,221,260,295
In recent years, the application of redox couples in SC-ISEs has received great attention due to the possibility of developing calibration-free SC-ISEs with high E0 reproducibility between electrodes. For instance, Zou et al. introduced a tris(phenanthroline) complex of Co(III) and Co(II) ([Co(phen)3]2+/[Co(phen)3]3+) into an ionophore-free PVC membrane and obtained a high E0 reproducibility (SD) of ±0.7 mV (n = 5) for K+-ISEs.140 Nevertheless, this redox-active organometallic complex cannot well maintain the high E0 reproducibility in ionophore-based SC-ISEs, and even if the lipophilicity is improved by using the tris(bipyridyl) complex of Co(III) and Co(II) ([Co(C9,C9-bipy)3]2+/[Co(C9,C9-bipy)3]3+) (Fig. 17a), a significant decrease in E0 reproducibility (±16.3 mV) is still obtained after one day of storage.251 This is because the redox couple composed of reduced and oxidized species is inevitably electrically charged and thus easily leaks into the sample solution as a result of ion exchange with primary ions. In addition, the large redox capacity of the transducer phase in these cases may increase the ion fluxes through the transducer/membrane interface, thereby resulting in a relatively high LOD of this type of SC-ISE. Based on these considerations, the group of Michalska introduced an idea of stabilizing the interfacial potential of SC-ISEs by incorporating the solid-contact layer with electrically neutral compounds, i.e., the cobalt(II) porphyrin/cobalt(III) corrole pair (Fig. 17b).252 This porphyrinoid complex can not only bind to the MWCNT surface via π–π stacking interactions, but also help to control ion fluxes due to the partial release of porphyrinoids into the membrane phase, thus resulting in additional beneficial effects on the analytical parameters (such as a low LOD of 10−8.3 M for K+). It is worth noting that although this compound contains two organometallic complexes of Co(II) and Co(III), they cannot be coupled to each other by an electrochemical means and thus they are not a redox couple. In addition, the Nernst equation is no longer applicable to directly predict the phase boundary potential on the back side of the ISM in this case. Later, the group of Bühlmann further added theoretical and experimental data to better clarify this cobalt(II) porphyrin/cobalt(III) corrole system.426 They provided a detailed theoretical derivation of the relationship between the interfacial potential and two mixed redox-active compounds and predicted that the ratio of pure oxidized/reduced species (not forming a redox couple) in the mixed compounds has little effect on the phase boundary potential, but even very small impurities in these species will lead to dramatic shifts. Combined with the experimental results, it is inferred that the key factor responsible for the remarkable E0 reproducibility may not be the presence of the oxidized and reduced species that do not form a redox couple, but rather the very small redox state impurities. Therefore, the authors suggested that the preparation of solid-contact layers containing both the oxidized and reduced species of a redox couple is still preferred for the development of calibration-free SC-ISEs.
 Fig. 17  (a) Schematic diagram of Co(III)/Co(II) redox couple-based SC-ISEs and the structural formula of cobalt(II/III) (4,4′-dinonyl-2,2′-bipyridyl). Reproduced with permission.251 Copyright 2014, American Chemical Society. (b) Schematic diagram of SC-ISEs based on the combination of cobalt(II) porphyrin/cobalt(III) corrole and CNTs.252 Reproduced with permission.252 Copyright 2017, American Chemical Society. (c) SEM image of TCNQ crystals.141 Reproduced with permission.141 Copyright 2015, American Chemical Society. (d) Cross-sectional SEM images of PVC membrane coated TTF- or TTF(NO3)-based solid-contact layers. Reproduced with permission.143 Copyright 2015, Electrochemical Society. (e) SEM image of TTF–TCNQ crystals. Reproduced with permission.256 Copyright 2018, Electrochemical Society. (f) SEM image of the TTF–GR composite. Reproduced with permission.253 Copyright 2016, Elsevier. (g) SEM image of the TTFCl–CB composite. Reproduced with permission.254 Copyright 2018, Elsevier. (h) SEM images of flower-like or long-tubular-like Au–TTF crystals. Reproduced with permission.255 Copyright 2019, Elsevier. 
In addition to the above-mentioned cobalt-based materials, TTF/TTF− and TCNQ/TCNQ− redox couples are also promising candidates for use as redox buffers to well control the interfacial potential of SC-ISEs. TTF and TCNQ are well-known conductive organic crystals with high electrical conductivity427 and have also long been used in the field of ion sensing.428–430 Recently, the group of Paczosa-Bator has developed a series of SC-ISEs based on TTF, TCNQ, and their free radical salts (Fig. 17c–e).141,143,256 The TTF-based NO3−-ISEs can achieve an E0 reproducibility (SD) of ±0.5 mV (n = 5),143 while the TCNQ-based Na+-ISEs exhibit an E0 reproducibility of ±1.2 mV (n = 5).141 Furthermore, a significant advantage of TTF and TCNQ is that they can be used to form composites with various carbon-based materials as solid-contact layers for SC-ISEs to obtain enhanced potential stability and reproducibility (Fig. 17f and g).253,254,258,259 In other cases, Xu et al. studied the effects of the morphologies of TTF-based charge-transfer compounds on their use as solid-contact layers (Fig. 17h).255 A shape-controlled Au–TTF hybrid crystal was in situ synthesized in microfluidic devices. Its long-tubular-like microstructure is found to be most suitable for the preparation of SC-ISEs due to its good chemical stability, the co-existence of TTF/TTF−, and its high redox capacitance. The group of Lindner found that although potential stability was significantly improved, the E0 deviation was found to be improved (±6 mV, n = 3) after the incorporation of the TCNQ/TCNQ− redox couple into the POT-based solid-contact layer.294 Therefore, they believed that the introduction of TCNQ salts containing the corresponding primary ions may be a better way to stabilize the interfacial potential. Hu et al. evaluated the performance of a redox buffer containing TCNQ/KTCNQ in CIMC-based Cl−-ISEs.257 A situation similar to the Co(II)/Co(III) redox couple was observed, in which the E0 reproducibility between electrodes significantly decreased after 24 h of conditioning, indicating that the ratio of TCNQ/KTCNQ present in the ISM changed. This situation may be thought of as acceptable for disposable paper-based sensors with short-time measurements.
So far, a variety of functional materials have been used to provide a reversible redox couple at the interface between the sensing membrane and the underlying conductive substrate. Except for the aforementioned types of materials, there are also redox-active SAMs based on C60 or TTF derivatives,135,136 ferrocene,137,138 hydroquinone/quinone,431 KBr/AgBr,260etc. Significant improvements resulting from the use of these functionalized materials for SC-ISEs have been obtained, however, they still need to be more fully convincing to make them more widely acceptable, especially to avoid or address the obvious shortcomings that have been identified. For instance, although redox-active SAMs based on C60 or TTF derivatives have been proved to be effective ion-to-electron transducers for stabilizing the potential response and inhibiting the formation of a water layer,135,136 the inherently low redox capacitance and limited stability are considered to be the limitations for their further applications.48 In another example, ferrocene as an ion-to-electron transducer is not only used in conventional potentiometry,137,138 but also in dynamical electrochemical ion sensing systems.106,432,433 Nonetheless, as further research has found that its oxidized form (i.e., ferrocenium ion) is unstable under certain circumstances,57,434–436 cautious consideration should be given when using ferrocene as the ion-to-electron transducer for SC-ISEs.344
3.6 Intercalation compounds
ICs have both ionic and electronic conductivities because of their unique properties of readily reversible intercalation and ion-exchange reactions, which make them promising for batteries, displays, and sensors.437 Alkali insertion materials have been proved to be suitable for the determination of the corresponding alkali ions, which is governed by the Nernst rule.438–441 However, the direct detection using ICs is susceptible to the interference of ions and redox species in the sample solution. Inspired by the wide range of studies on ICs as the electrode materials for rechargeable batteries, Komaba et al. presented their implementation as solid-contact layers for SC-ISEs.442 They evaluated the performance of lithium, sodium, and potassium insertion materials as ion-to-electron transducers for SC-ISEs and proved the improvements in stabilizing the membrane potential and reducing the interfacial resistance. Schuhmann et al. further studied the electrochemical equilibria and potential distribution of IC-based SC-ISEs.142 They demonstrated that SC-ISEs based on target-ion ICs can yield well-defined and reproducible standard potentials, e.g., the Li+-ISEs using LiFePO4/FePO4 as the solid-contact layer exhibit a high E0 reproducibility between electrodes (±2.0 mV, n = 3) and a high potential stability (SD) of ±1.5 mV (n = 9) measured in 10−1 M LiCl solution on the 42nd day. The reversible (de-)intercalation process of LiFePO4 can occur over a wide range of Li+ concentrations with a very flat potential plateau, which provides benefits for achieving well-defined interfacial potential and high redox capacity with low polarization as the ion-to-electron transducer. Because of the chemical stability and the constant activity of primary ions in the IC-based solid-contact layer, in the ideal case, the membrane potential will only depend on the primary ion activity in the sample solution. A detailed theoretical derivation of potential formation and standard potential E0 has also been provided in this work.142 Following this work, Komaba et al. verified the possibility of using ICs intercalated with other ions as solid-contact layers to develop the corresponding SC-ISEs (Fig. 18).261 Three alkali insertion materials, LiFePO4, Na0.33MnO2, and KxMnO2·nH2O, were used as solid-contact layers for the fabrication of the corresponding SC-ISEs. The efficient stabilization of the membrane potential and the reduced electrode impedance enable these SC-ISEs to possess a fast potential response (<5 s) and improved potentiometric performance. It is also found that the combination of the PVC sensing membrane can protect these IC-based solid-contact layers from interference factors in the analyte solution and improve their sensitivity and selectivity. In addition, Kojima et al. developed a minimally invasive glucose monitoring system composed of an Na+-ISE based on an insertion material (Na0.33MnO2) and an enzyme-based glucose sensor for estimating glucose levels in the blood.443
 Fig. 18  Schematic illustration of the interfacial charge transfer process in the Pt/ISM (left) and Pt/insertion materials/ISM (right). Reproduced with permission.261 Copyright 2017, Royal Society of Chemistry. 
3.7 Prussian blue and its analogues
Prussian blue (PB), which is known to be the oldest known coordination polymer, has long been used in the field of ion sensing.444–447 PBAs possess the general crystallographic structure, but their chemical composition changes.448 In 2005, Gabrielli et al. tried to used a PB film as the ion-to-electron transducer for K+-ISEs.139 Although these PB-based SC-ISEs do not show an ideal Nernstian potential response, these types of SC-ISEs can be used to study the kinetics at the membrane|solution interface and to clarify the role of the PVC membrane. Later, Ocypa et al. used HCF anion doped PEDOT as the solid-contact layer to construct Cu2+-ISEs.449 They found that the Cu2+ cation can spontaneously accumulate in the solid-contact layer through transmembrane transfer, thus resulting in super-Nernstian behaviors. Besides, the HCF anion was also used as the doping agent in PPY, which was intended to act as a redox buffer to enhance the potential stability of SC-ISEs.311,450,451 Following these earlier studies, the group of Mikhelson studied the possibility of using CuHCF containing Fe2+/Fe3+ as the solid-contact layer for K+-ISEs.262 The authors found that although this material has both ion-exchange and redox properties, the E0 reproducibility between electrodes and long-term potential stability of this type of SC-ISE are far from their liquid-contact counterparts. Ghosh et al. constructed Na+-ISEs based on chitosan and PB (CS–PB) nanocomposites, which combine the double-layer capacitance of chitosan and the redox capacitance of PB.263 The CS–PB-enabled solid-contact layer possesses a high contact interfacial area with the sensing membrane due to its macroporous structure. However, this kind of SC-ISE seems to suffer from the effect of the formation of a water layer.
In addition, PB and PBAs have an attractive feature, i.e., certain size-specific ions can be reversibly embedded into the large interstitial sites inside their face-centered cubic structure.452,453 Based on this unique property, the group of Schuhmann reported the employment of PBAs as solid-contact layers for the development of SC-ISEs (Fig. 19).264 Three K+-intercalated PBAs (K-CuHCF, K-NiHCF, and K-FeHCF), one Na+-intercalated PBA (Na-NiHCF), and one Ca2+-intercalated PBA (Ca-NiHCF) were used as the solid-contact layers for the corresponding K+-, Na+-, and Ca2+-ISEs, respectively. These PBA-based SC-ISEs exhibit a reproducible potential response over a period of months and possess a similar sensitivity and selectivity compared to those of their liquid-contact counterparts. Interestingly, it is found that PBA-based solid-contact layers can show predictable and adjustable standard potentials by altering the properties and redox states of the precursors during the synthesis process of PBAs.
 Fig. 19  Schematic illustration of the interfacial potential in the SC-ISEs based on target cation intercalated PBAs. Reproduced with permission.264 Copyright 2017, Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH & Co. KGaA, Weinheim. 
3.8 Ionic liquids
Ionic liquids (ILs) are composed of organic salts that remain in the liquid state below 100 °C, even below ambient temperature, and offer tunable physicochemical properties by modifying the cation and the anion according to the specific requirements of the desired functional materials or solvents.454 Our group synthesized a kind of task-specific IL, called N,N,N-trimethylaniline hexafluorophosphate (NTHP), and employed it as the ion-to-electron transducer for K+-ISEs.265 Because of the presence of the aniline-functionalized cation and hexafluorophosphate anion, this material has both redox and hydrophobic properties. The obtained SC-ISEs exhibit a potential drift of 34 µV h−1 over 20 h and are resistant to environmental interferences. In other studies, the group of Wardak developed chloride IL-based SC-ISEs, which have a two-layer PVC membrane structure.455 The inner layer of the SC-ISEs contains chloride IL doped plasticized PVC and connects with the Ag/AgCl electrode, whereas the outer layer is the commonly used PVC-based ISM. These chloride ILs are used as sources of Cl− to keep constant Cl− concentration in the inner membrane phase, thereby ensuring the potential stability of the internal reference electrode. Based on this structure, a series of SC-ISEs have been developed for the detection of heavy metal ions in real sample solutions.266,267,456,457 When the inner layer contained an IL (1-ethyl-3-methylimidazolium chloride, EMImCl), no significant potential drift was observed during the water layer test, and the long-term potential stability was about 0.1 mV per day.267 However, the possible leaching of ILs from the PVC phase into the sample solution is considered to be an adverse factor for these SC-ISEs.458
Based on the intrinsic properties of ILs (such as hydrophobicity, electrochemical stability, electrical conductivity, and low melting point), their application in SC-ISEs is more than just as the solid-contact layers. For example, the use of IL as an effective binder can enhance the adhesion between the solid-contact layer based on a carbo nanomaterial (SWCNTs or GR) and the GC electrode substrate.459 In addition, room temperature ILs have also been applied as the polymeric membrane compositions, such as ionic additives, plasticizers, and even ionophores.460–466 Low-melting ILs with a melting point above room temperature can be used as a sensing layer matrix alternative to conventional plasticized polymeric membranes for SC-ISEs.467–471 For more details about these applications of ILs in SC-ISEs, refer to several good published review articles (ref. 24, 61, 344 and 472).
3.9 Others
Apart from the aforementioned functional materials, some other materials with high specific surface area or high redox activity can also be used as solid-contact layers for SC-ISEs. For instance, black phosphorus (BP) is a relatively stable one among the three main allotropic forms of phosphorus.473 As a non-carbon and non-metallic material, BP has a high surface-to-volume ratio and charge carrier mobility. Kou et al. estimated the performance characteristics of BP-based Ca2+-ISEs.268 The prepared SC-ISEs exhibit enhanced potential stability with an LOD of 4.0 × 10−7 M. No obvious water layer formation and gas and light interference are observed in this work. The presence of a sensing membrane is thought to enhance the stability of BP and prevent its slow chemical degradation. For further increasing the long-term stability and hydrophobicity of BP, Yang et al. prepared a composite material of ERGO coated BP (BP/ERGO) and used it as the solid-contact layer for the fabrication of BP/ERGO-based Ca2+-ISEs (Fig. 20a).269
 Fig. 20  (a) SEM image of the BP/RGO composite. Reproduced with permission.269 Copyright 2019, ESG. (b) SEM image of MOF (Ni3HHTP2) nanocrystallites. Reproduced with permission.270 Copyright 2018, American Chemical Society. (c) TEM image of MXene (Ti3C2Tx) nanosheets. Reproduced with permission.271 Copyright 2019, Springer Nature. (d) SEM image of MoS2 nanoflowers. Reproduced with permission.272 Copyright 2016, Elsevier. (e) A POT–MoS2 based SC-ISE fabricated with the use of an automatic fluid dispenser for the measurement of NO3− in soil samples. (f) The fabricated SC-ISE exhibits comparable analytical performance with the commercial sensors in real soil sample tests. Reproduced with permission.273 Copyright 2019, American Chemical Society. 
In addition, some novel metal-based nanomaterials, such as conductive metal–organic frameworks (MOFs) and MXene, due to some unique characteristics, have also been tried as solid contact layers in SC-ISEs. MOFs are crystalline coordination polymers with highly porous structures.474,475 Mendecki and Mirica verified the possibility using of three different MOFs (Ni3HHTP2, Cu3HHTP2, and Co3HHTP2) as ion-to-electron transducers for SC-ISEs (Fig. 20b).270 Among them, Ni3HHTP2 is proved to have the highest bulk capacitance by the EIS measurement and is used to fabricate solid-contact K+-ISEs. The authors also pointed out that the capacitance of SC-ISEs is limited by the instinct porosity and conductivity of the MOFs used, which can still be further improved. Recently, our group has utilized two MXene (Ti3C2Tx and Ti2CTx) nanosheets to fabricate solid-contact Ca2+-ISEs (Fig. 20c).271 MXene nanosheets possess high specific surface areas, characterized by their high capacitance. These MXene-based SC-ISEs exhibit a higher double-layer capacitance than their counterparts with CRGO-enabled transducers.203
MoS2 nanoflowers are a metal sulfide nanomaterial with a high specific surface area and have been proved to be an effective ion-to-electron transducer for SC-ISEs by the group of Qin (Fig. 20d).272 The prepared MoS2 nanoflower-based K+-ISEs exhibit similar potentiometric characteristics to their MoO2 microsphere-based counterparts.244 The transduction mechanism of the MoS2 nanoflower-enabled transducer is based on the formation of a double-layer capacitance at the SC|ISM interface. In another work, Ali and coworkers presented a miniaturized potentiometric nitrate sensing device containing a pair of SC-ISE and RE for long-term soil analysis (Fig. 20e and f).273 The MoS2 nanosheet doped POT (POT–MoS2) composite material is applied as the ion-to-electron transducer for SC-ISEs. The incorporation of MoS2 into the POT chain is conducive to improving the conductivity and anion exchange ability to obtain enhanced redox capacitance. A high-precision automatic dispenser machine is used to support the assembly of sensors, which can well control the solution distribution of the MoS2–POT composite and sensing membrane. These POT–MoS2-enabled SC-ISEs show a wide detection range, covering all concentrations of NO3− related to agricultural applications, and practical application potential to continuously monitor nitrate in the real samples of soil slurries for up to 27 days.
4. New development trends
The generation of modern ISEs is accompanied by the pursuit of miniaturization, resulting in ion-selective microelectrodes (ISMEs). As a miniature version of the original macro design, ISMEs can be more adequate for some demanding conditions, such as a sample solution with confined volume or measurement in living organisms.34,476 On the other hand, in vivo organ monitoring and integration with miniaturized wearable devices require the flexibility of these microsensors.477,478 Diversified needs are continually driving the development of ISEs toward miniaturization and flexibility. Although conventional liquid-contact ISEs can be scaled down to a low micron size,44 these miniaturized liquid-contact ISEs are rather fragile, complicated, and difficult to standardize and mass produce, limiting their manufacture and applications.295 For SC-ISEs, it is commonly identified that the introduction of solid-contact functional materials is beneficial for their miniaturization and flexibility. The diversity of solid-contact functional materials and substrate selection offer the miniaturized and flexible SC-ISEs more development possibilities. Moreover, their compatibility with modern microfabrication and array construction technologies allows them to be economically produced on a larger scale. On the basis of these advantages, a variety of miniaturized and flexible SC-ISEs have been developed for the detection of ion activities in different matrixes. These microsensors are extremely attractive due to their compact size, less maintenance requirements, and outstanding analysis parameters, showing great potential for completely replacing their liquid-contact counterparts and even their original macro-design. Therefore, the development of miniaturized and flexible SC-ISEs has become an important new development trend in the field of potentiometric ion sensing.
4.1 Miniaturized SC-ISEs
In routine potentiometric analysis, the size of polymeric membrane-based ISEs is usually not limited by the operating environment and the available sample volume. Generally, the conventional ISEs typically have a millimeter-level sensing surface with a pencil-like size. However, when attempting to determine ion activities in a finite sample volume, e.g., a small amount of blood or sweat, or even within a single intact cell, such a large sensor configuration is obviously not desirable. In this context, ISMEs show their particular attractiveness for trace-level analysis in confined samples. Compared with other analytical techniques, potentiometry with ISEs does not consume a large amount of analyte and, in principle, the potential generated is directly related to the primary ion activity in the sample solution, not to the sample volume.104 The growing demands for in vivo measurements and smaller systems of analytical devices are also important motivations for the miniaturization of SC-ISEs.

4.1.1 Design and structure. 
In retrospect, micron-sized ISMEs based on polymeric membranes have long been used for in vivo applications dating back to 1975, when Thomas et al. described a micropipette-based liquid-contact ISME for direct measurement of intracellular Li+ ions in snail neurons.479 These early liquid-contact ISMEs were commonly made of borosilicate glass micropipettes, which were derived from the improvements on one of Walker's methods,480 and have also been widely applied to various areas for ion sensing.481–486 Some summary reviews or books have been published on their development and applications.44,487–491 However, the disadvantages of these micropipette-based ISMEs are just as obvious, such as difficulty in their preparation, high electrical resistance, short life span of only a few hours or days, and vulnerability to mechanical contact or electric shock. Thus, optimizing electrode structure design to increase durability is very critical for the development of ISMEs. One of the most attractive approaches is to introduce internal solid-contact layers to replace conventional inner filling solutions. For typical micropipette-based solid-contact ISMEs (SC-ISMEs), the inner filling solution and internal reference electrode are replaced by functional material modified conductive wires inserted into the membrane cocktail.492 Besides, the introduction of solid-contact functional materials allows ISMEs to be manufactured as other smaller structures, such as the needle-like design shown in Fig. 21a.493,494 The use of the solid-contact configuration also means that there is no need for any optimizations related to inner filling solutions, or for considering the difficulties caused by undesired transmembrane ion fluxes. The advantages of mechanical robustness and durability of SC-ISMEs allow them to be used in a wider range of applications.
 Fig. 21  (a) A comparison between needle-shaped SC-ISMEs and micropipette-based liquid-contact ISMEs. Reproduced with permission.493,494 Copyright 2009, Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH & Co. KGaA, Weinheim. Copyright 2008, Elsevier. (b) Microfabricated planar Christmas tree-shaped microelectrode arrays (12 × 4 mm). Inset: Magnified view of a sensor tip. Reproduced with permission.504 Copyright 2001, American Chemical Society. 
Benefiting from the advances in the original macro-design, various SC-ISMEs with higher robustness have been developed. Initially, the main aim of research on SC-ISMEs is to improve the structure of micropipette-based liquid-contact ISMEs. For example, Gyurcsányi et al. firstly tried to fabricate a solid-contact K+-ISME based on a PPY-modified conductive substrate (a metal wire or carbon fiber with different diameters sealed in a glass capillary).495 However, it is difficult to control the specific sensing area on the microfabricated disk electrode substrate through a direct drop-casting method. Therefore, the same group put forward an improved structure design through accommodating both the PEDOT film and the membrane cocktail into a recessed microcavity (25 µm diameter) formed by chemically etching the gold wire sealed in the glass capillary, thereby precisely controlling the area of the sensing surface and mechanically protecting it from the analyte environment.496 Later, Shim and coworkers proposed a similar configuration protocol.497 A glass capillary with a conical nanopore structure (less than 0.5 µm diameter) served as a mechanically robust container for the fabrication of SC-ISMEs, in which the membrane cocktails and hydrogel were distributed onto the Ag/AgCl-deposited Pt nanopore electrode. These improved microelectrodes described above all have small micron-scale sensing areas, but the overall size is still relatively large, and so they are commonly used in flowing systems or as potentiometric scanning electrochemical microscopy (SECM) probes. In addition, since these SC-ISMEs are still based on glass micropipettes, extra attention should be paid to their fragility when used.
In other cases, the preparation of microelectrodes is no longer dependent on conventional glass micropipettes. The elimination of the inner filling solution allows SC-ISMEs to be prepared without any liquid containers. For example, Lamaka et al. reported a microelectrode configuration protocol similar to the original macro-design of the CWE, in which SC-ISMEs were constructed by sequentially depositing the POT films and ISM cocktails onto the exposed apex of an insulated needle-shaped Pt–Ir alloy wire (Fig. 21a).493 Before depositing the solid-contact layer, a layer of gold was electrodeposited on the exposed apex to ensure stable adherence. Two types of SC-IdSMEs with a less than 10 µm sensing portion length were fabricated for the detection of H+ and Mg2+. These SC-ISMEs are designed to contain neither liquid nor highly fragile components, and thus they are more robust and durable than their conventional glass micropipette-based counterparts. Meanwhile, their reasonably short response time makes them available for local potentiometric SECM measurements in biomedical and corrosion science applications. However, the authors also mentioned that the preparation of such microelectrodes is not always successful due to the possible initial defects in the solid-contact and/or membrane layer. Later, the same group used a plasticizer-free MMA–DMA membrane to further improve their design of a needle-shaped microelectrode.498 Solid-contact H+-ISMEs were constructed and utilized as SECM probes for corrosion monitoring, exhibiting good potentiometric behaviors. Moreover, these SC-ISMEs can be used in SCEM measurements continuously for more than 24 hours and have a lifespan of up to 5 months.
More importantly, the use of solid-contact functional materials is compatible with mass production technology, making them particularly attractive. Different SC-ISMEs have been constructed by using thin-film (e.g., photolithographic) or thick-film (e.g., screen printing) methods to pattern conductive substrates and solid-contact layers, with the use of an automatic microdispenser to dispense the membrane cocktails. For example, Lindner and Buck developed a series of planar SC-ISME array on flexible PI substrates based on existing semiconductor and microelectronics technologies.499–503 As shown in Fig. 21b, these microelectrode arrays were constructed based on poly-HEMA (2-hydroxyethyl methacrylate) hydrogel interlayers and polymeric membranes and could be used for the in vivo detection of H+, Na+, K+, and Ca2+.504 This group also provided detailed discussions about the thin- and thick-film fabrication processes for mass production of SC-ISMEs.34,505
To date, different SC-ISMEs have been developed and applied for potentiometric ion sensing under specific conditions. These miniaturized sensors have been demonstrated to achieve nanomolar LOD in confined samples and possess a lifespan of up to months. The compatibility with modern microfabrication and array construction technologies and the diverse selection of solid-contact functional materials and conductive substrates allow SC-ISMEs to be easily designed and mass-produced, endowing them with a unique appeal. Based on different ionophore-based polymeric membranes, SC-ISMEs with different selectivity can be prepared and integrated. However, as the dimensions of SC-ISMEs further decrease, the precision requirement of micro-machining technology will increase and the uncertainty of their analytical performance will also inevitably increase. Some of the factors that affect the analytical performance of the ISEs are exacerbated in their miniaturized versions, such as the leaching of active components in the membrane, poor membrane adhesion due to a smaller contact area, the formation of a water layer and a pH change resulting from the transmembrane transport of water and gas. Therefore, the key to the design of SC-ISMEs is to take full account of the required analytical parameters and select appropriate configuration protocols to achieve a balance between their size and performance. Various fabrication processes correspond to different standards and product parameters, and researchers should choose the appropriate one according to their specific demands. Moreover, stricter design criteria must be followed to ensure these microsensors can achieve comparable or even better performance characteristics to their original-bulk or liquid-contact counterparts. Anyway, it can be believed that the continuous development of microfabrication technologies provides more choice for the manufacture of SC-ISMEs and makes possible the production of SC-ISMEs with uniform performance in a more convenient and economical manner.


4.1.2 Potentiometric scanning measurement. 
On the basis of these structural and performance studies, SC-ISEMs have now been used in various matrixes to monitor ion concentrations. Among them, an important application scenario for SC-ISMEs is to act as SECM probes. SECM is a scanning probe technology that quantifies the local material flux from a surface with a high spatial and temporal resolution,506 such as studying localized metal corrosion processes or the transmembrane ion flux of liquid-contact ISEs.507,508 The ability to measure a specific ion activity at the solid|liquid interface from the solution side makes ISMEs suitable for use as scanning probes in the potentiometric SECM mode, which is also known as the scanning ion-selective electrode technique (SIET).507 Ever since the applicability of ISMEs for SECM measurements was successfully demonstrated,509,510 a series of efforts have been made in this field to develop more robust and durable potentiometric SECM probes, especially the introduction of a solid-contact layer provides a new choice for configuration protocols.511 Among them, one of the most reported configuration protocols for SC-ISMEs is based on inserting the PEDOT coated carbon fibers into the backfilled polymeric membrane cocktails in the glass micropipette tips. This method has a high success rate in the preparation of microelectrodes based on micropipettes, because there is no need to worry about the air bubbles that may be caused when the internal electrolyte backfilled into the micropipette, and the insertion step of carbon fiber is relatively easy.512 Based on this method, a variety of micropipette-based SC-ISMESs have been developed as SECM probes for the local concentration distribution detection of NH4+,512,513 K+,514 Mg2+,492,515–517 Zn2+,518,519 and Cu2+.520 Due to the introduction of solid-contact layers, these solid-contact micropipette electrodes have a lower electrical resistance and faster response than their conventional liquid-contact counterparts of the same size. As a result, higher scanning rates can be used in the potentiometric SECM mode to obtain higher quality SECM imaging without the need for special electric shielding.521,522 Moreover, they also have lower maintenance requirements and longer service life.
Monitoring metal corrosion using the SIET is a common area, in which SC-ISMEs are used as SECM probes to quantitatively map the local changes in pH and metallic cation concentration during the metal corrosion process. For example, Izquierdo et al. fabricated a micropipette-based Mg2+-ISME for monitoring galvanic corrosion processes in the potentiometric SECM mode.492 Compared with conventional liquid-contact counterparts previously reported,523 these prepared SC-ISMEs improve the SECM images of Mg2+ concentration distribution with a high spatial resolution due to their lower internal resistance and faster response time.
