Besides, SC-ISMEs can also be combined together or combined with other microelectrodes to form a double- or multi-barrel assembly for simultaneous monitoring of ion distribution.524–526 For example, Filotás et al. constructed a double-barrel microelectrode to simultaneously detect local changes in pH and Zn2+ concentration in the potentiometric SECM mode (Fig. 22a) and extended this structure to obtain 2D maps of Cu2+ and Zn2+ ions by combining a Cu2+-ISME.520 In addition, Ummadi et al. reported a dual-function Ca2+-ISME, which can be used as a potentiometric SECM probe to detect Ca2+ distribution or record the amperometric approach curve to determine the distance between the probe tip and the substrate surface.527 This microelectrode was constructed based on a borosilicate capillary, in which conductive Vulcan carbon powder was used as a component of the PVC membrane cocktail and the Vulcan carbon/bis(2-ethylhexyl)sebacate (DOS) composite was used as to connect the inserted copper wire. Electrochemical characterization demonstrated the good potentiometric behaviors of the Ca2+-ISME, including a near Nernstian response slope of 28 ± 2 mV per decade, a low LOD of 1 µM, and a fast response time of ∼0.2 s. This Ca2+-ISME was used to quantitatively map Ca2+ distribution release from a bioactive glass dental composite.
 Fig. 22  (a) Double-barrel microelectrode for potentiometric SECM imaging of galvanic corrosion reactions. Reproduced with permission.520 Copyright 2017, Elsevier. (b) Two types of SC-ISMEs for MIFE measurement. Reproduced with permission.530 Copyright 2018, Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH & Co. KGaA, Weinheim. 
In addition, SC-ISMEs are also used in another scanning technique called microelectrode ion flux estimation (MIFE), which can be used to non-invasively study the kinetics of transmembrane ion fluxes in organisms.528,529 For instance, Church and coworkers fabricated solid-contact Zn2+-ISMEs to in situ study the transport processes of Zn2+ in the foliage and roots of sour orange seedlings using the non-invasive MIFE technique (Fig. 22b).530 Two configurations of SC-ISMEs were constructed based on a commercially available micropipette (tip size: 540 µm diameter) or a borosilicate glass micropipette (tip size: 40 µm diameter), respectively. The PVC-based Zn2+-ISM was connected with the POT coated gold wires. Electrochemical characterization demonstrated that the prepared POT-based Zn2+-ISMEs with different tip sizes show similar potentiometric response behaviors with the LOD at the micromolar level. The developed Zn2+-ISMEs were used to study the Zn2+ transport processes through monitoring the decrease in ion concentration on the surface of plant tissues as a result of ion uptake by living cells.


4.1.3 Microelectrode array for multiple ion analysis. 
One advantage of microfabrication is that SC-ISMEs with different selectivities can be integrated onto the same planar or three-dimensional miniaturized sensing platform using the same or only slightly modified manufacturing steps. The miniaturized configuration allows these devices to accommodate more sensors in a limited space, enabling a more complete analysis of the target analyte, which is very desirable for certain complex matrixes, such as sweat, blood, and urine. In this context, the group of Diamond proposed a hydrogel-based ISME array device, which can be used to simultaneously monitor Na+ and Cl− in a concentration range related to the diagnosis of cystic fibrosis (CF) in sweat.531 The microelectrode array was packaged into a flow cell with a volume of 40 µL. The group of Lewenstam described a method to simultaneously perform potentiometric measurements of Na+, K+, Ca2+, Cl−, and pH of blood electrolytes in a one-drop serum sample.532 The sample droplet (less than 30 µL) can be spontaneously entrapped between the microscope glass cover-slip and the flat front section of the potentiometric probe (with built-in SC-ISMEs and REs) by adhesion forces to avoid evaporation and enable rapid determination.
For multiple ion detection in human biofluids for physiological analysis, an attractive approach is the development of multi-sensor platforms based on flow injection or microfluidics. For example, Toczyłowska-Mamińska et al. constructed a flow-injection platform integrated with an SC-ISME array, aiming to simultaneously determine physiologically important ions (Na+, K+, Cl−, and pH) in the cell monolayer and tissue.533 These SC-ISMEs were prepared on Ag/AgCl electrodes with plasticized PU-based ISMs, coupled with an IL-based RE to perform potentiometric measurements. The successful measurement of ion fluxes in the human colonic epithelial Caco-2 cell line proves the design rationality of this device. Moya and coworkers built a modular sensing platform for simultaneous multi-analyte monitoring in biofluids, which integrated solid-contact Na+- and K+-ISMEs, as well as dissolved oxygen and pH sensors (Fig. 23a).534 As a proof-of-concept, this device was successfully used to assess the real mice urine on different diets, proving its practical potential in complex biological matrixes. Furthermore, its high versatility and low sample volume requirement (0.83 µL) make this device also suitable for different microfluidic cell culture systems to monitor multiple chemicals in real time. Moon and Farzbod proposed a digital electrowetting-on-dielectric (EWOD) droplet-based microfluidic platform with a SC-ISME array (Fig. 23b).535 Attractively, these SC-ISMEs were seamlessly integrated with a digital platform through an on-chip fabrication protocol. With EWOD drop-based microfluidics, the on-chip fabrication process of SC-ISMEs includes chemically oxidizing electroplated silver to form an AgCl layer and depositing the membrane cocktail to prepare the ISM. The advantages of ease of use, automation, and low reagent consumption enable this platform to have the potential for use as a portable home-use ion monitoring device.
 Fig. 23  (a) A SC-ISME-based microfluidic platform for the simultaneous measurement of Na+ and K+ concentration, dissolved oxygen, and pH in real urine samples. Reproduced with permission.534 Copyright 2018, Elsevier. (b) A digital EWOD droplet-based microfluidic platform. Reproduced with permission.535 Copyright 2018, Elsevier. (c) An endoscopic probe with an SC-ISME array for simultaneously monitoring extracellular pH and K+ to identify tissue ischemia. Reproduced with permission.537 Copyright 2014, Elsevier. (d) SC-ISME array based rigid or flexible diagnostic platforms for biofluid analysis and tissue ischemia assessment. Reproduced with permission.539 Copyright 2018, Elsevier. (e) An SC-ISME chip platform for in vitro intracellular recording (left). SEM image of a micropipette filled with the sensing membrane cocktail (right). Reproduced with permission.540 Copyright 2005, Elsevier. (f) A micropipette-based SC-ISME platform for cell culture (left). The SC-ISME array is located at the bottom of the main microchannel (right). Inset: SEM close-up of the micropipette (2 µm diameter). Reproduced with permission.543 Copyright 2006, American Chemical Society. (g) A cell electrophysiology biochip (centre chip size: 9 × 11 mm) for in silico potentiometric Ca2+ measurements. This device is mounted on a PCB with a plastic reservoir and 64 op-amps. Inset: Optical images of the pyramidal pores and surrounding insulating layer. Reproduced with permission.545 Copyright 2007, Elsevier. 
In addition, these microelectrode array devices can also be used as auxiliary medical tools for the monitoring of the condition of tissues or organs. For instance, Zine et al. fabricated a needle-shaped PPY-based H+-ISME planar array to monitor organs during cardiac surgery or transplant transportation.536 Tahirbegi and coworkers developed microelectrode array probes for endoscopic surgery to identify the occurrence of ischemia after gastrointestinal anastomosis (Fig. 23c).537 This potentiometric probe was composed of a 12-microelectrode array for simultaneously monitoring pH and K+ in the anastomotic region under ischemia. The conception feasibility was verified by testing inside the stomach of the pig, revealing that this device has a certain tolerance to acidic conditions. Besides, the introduction of PEDOT has been proved to further improve the analytical performance of these microelectrodes.538 The group of Yang proposed a point-of-care diagnostic platform for the assessment of tissue ischemia, which can be used to measure K+, Na+, and pH in different liquid samples (Fig. 23d).539 The realization of different SC-ISMEs is based on the standardized PCB manufacturing technique, which is a promising approach to produce low-cost, mass-produced, multi-parametric chemical sensing diagnostic platforms. Two rigid sensing platforms with 34-microelectrode arrays were developed to perform in vitro liquid sample dip-stick analysis. Furthermore, flexible sensing platforms have also been extended, which are intended to be wrapped as a ring and placed within the intestinal lumen to assess tissue ischemia after surgical anastomosis.
Another important application field of microelectrode arrays is the establishment of a lab-on-a-chip platform for monitoring cell culture. For example, Guenat and coworkers presented a sophisticated SC-ISME array platform aimed at in vitro intracellular recording (Fig. 23e).540 The entire device platform is mounted on a PCB, including a glass chip with microchannels and a silicon chip with a 24-microelectrode array. The SC-ISMEs were constructed by filling the silicon nitride micropipettes (5 µm inner diameter) with the membrane cocktails. The micropipette geometry provides reproducible and clearly defined membrane thickness and effective sensing area with good mechanical anchorage. These microsensors can operate in the range of 10−6–10−1 M Ca2+ with a slope of 27 mV per decade. Through the improvement of micromachining technology, the inner diameter of the micropipette can be further down to 250 nm.541 Based on micropipette-based SC-ISMEs, the same group also developed a generic platform for cell culture that enabled real-time monitoring of extracellular ion activities to reflect cell states (e.g., necrosis, apoptosis, or differentiation) (Fig. 23f).542,543 Two kinds of micropipette-based SC-ISMEs were manufactured and installed at the bottom of the microwell for cultured cells to determine the levels of K+ and NH4+ in cell cultures. Besides, this platform was also used to study the early signs of induced cell lysis for cytotoxicity assays, by using extracellular K+ as a marker of cell death.544 Inspired by Guenat's work, the group of Porterfield designed a lab-on-chip system, which is expected to perform fern spore Ca2+ measurements in ground studies or microgravity flight experiments (Fig. 23g).545 This biochip was microfabricated on a silicon substrate, consisting of a 64-microelectrode array leading into 16 pyramidal pores (150 µm × 150 µm) that were specially designed according to the general size of the target cell and acted as measurement units in themselves. Coupled with specific data acquisition and processing technology, the application potential of this biochip as an essential tool for basic cell biology research was preliminarily demonstrated by measuring Ca2+ released from germinated fern spores. The same group also developed a coin-sized multianalyte biochip for physiological sensing in a liquid environment.546 They found that the introduction of PEDOT as the ion-to-electron transducer can improve the analytical performance and lifespan of these SC-ISMEs in this biochip.


4.1.4 
            In situ water environment analysis. 
SC-ISMEs are attractive, small, and convenient analytical tools for in situ determination of various ions in a volume-limited aqueous sample without the need for sample pretreatment. Their high sensitivity and selectivity, as well as their ability to achieve an LOD at the nanomolar level, make them more competitive in water environment analysis than other sophisticated analytical tools.547,548 For example, the determination of heavy metal ions in coastal sediment pore water is of great importance to elucidate their impacts on water quality and the biogeochemical environment. When using SC-ISMEs to fine-scale measure heavy metal ions in sediment pore water, they can avoid perturbing their vertical distribution profiles. For example, Zhao and coworkers developed an SC-ISME and successfully applied it for in situ determination of Pb2+ in coastal sediment pore water.549 This type of SC-ISME was constructed by sequentially depositing the PEDOT/PSS-based solid-contact layer and the membrane cocktail on a gold wire (14 µm diameter) sealed in a glass capillary with an exposed tip. Due to this design, these SC-ISMEs are more robust than conventional liquid-contact counterparts and therefore more suitable for in situ pore water measurements. Remarkably, these prepared SC-ISMEs exhibited a low LOD of 6.4 × 10−10 M for Pb2+. Based on the same configuration protocol, changing the doped ionophores in the polymeric membranes can result in different SC-ISMEs, e.g., a Cu2+-ISME was also constructed for heavy metal ion analysis in sediments with a low LOD of 4.0 × 10−8 M.550
In other cases, SC-ISMEs can also be used for the in situ potentiometric ion measurement of river water or seawater samples. For example, the group of Diamond developed a pen-like multi-sensor potentiometric probe and successfully used it to in situ determine the pH of river water samples.551 An obvious advantage of this device is its multi-sensor configuration, which can be extended to the detection of other target ions. Xu and coworkers constructed a solid-contact Ca2+-ISME for continuous in situ seawater measurements.552 To prepare this SC-ISME, a Pt wire (0.5 mm diameter) was electropolymerized with the PEDOT/PSS layer and then coated with the membrane cocktail. The obtained SC-ISME has a certain degree of corrosion resistance to seawater and can maintain a lifespan of at least six months.


4.1.5 
            In vivo biomedical applications. 
SC-ISMEs have a number of applications in the biomedical field, especially for in vivo measurements. Due to the relative maturity of the preparation technology, various SC-ISMEs based on glass micropipettes are still the common analysis tools in this field. For example, Kim et al. constructed a solid-contact Ca2+-ISME for monitoring the dynamic changes in Ca2+ levels in the rat kidneys.553 This microsensor was made of a theta-type glass capillary with an Ag wire, which was treated to obtain a silanized Ag/AgCl surface and then coated with the membrane cocktail to prepare a Ca2+-ISME. A stable Nernstian response of 25.7 mV per decade was observed for the Ca2+-ISME. Furthermore, they also prepared a Pt wire-based amperometric NO microelectrode and combined it with the Ca2+-ISME to form a dual-function microsensor. Two different regions of a kidney, i.e., renal medulla and cortex, were selected to perform the location-dependent Ca2+ and NO analysis using the developed dual-function microsensor, and the results showed that the levels of Ca2+ and NO in the medulla are higher than those in the cortex. In addition, based on the same configuration protocols, an electrochemical dual-functional microsensor for the simultaneous determination of K+ and NO in rat brains under epileptic seizure was also developed by the same group.554
Compared with routine analysis, the application conditions of SC-ISMEs for in vivo measurements are more demanding and challenging, which puts forward higher requirements for SC-ISMEs. For example, these SC-ISMEs for in vivo measurements must be mechanically strong enough to penetrate the biological tissues and must be small enough to avoid unnecessary damage during insertion. Therefore, there is an urgent need to develop novel SC-ISMEs that are more robust, versatile, and insensitive to physicochemical factors to replace the conventional glass micropipette-based ones. For this, Odijk and coworkers developed a solid-contact K+-ISME probe with a novel design, which can be used to measure K+ levels in the living rodent brains at multiple depths and locations (Fig. 24a–c).555 Two microfabricated silicon probes of 100 µm × 100 µm square shaft diameter were mounted on a PCB, separated by 2 mm, which can be inserted in the rat brains for simultaneous measurements at two locations. Both microprobes have seven Pt microelectrode substrates, of which the diameter of tetrode structure microelectrode disks is 20 µm and the diameter of the other three disks is 10 µm, and SiO2 is deposited to insulate the lead of the Pt microelectrodes. A layer of PEDOT was electrochemically polymerized on the surface of the microelectrode disks to form the solid-contact layer, which was then covered with the K+-sensitive membrane cocktails to prepare K+-ISMEs. Typical membranes have a thickness of 5 µm in the middle and a thickness of 15 µm at the edge. As a proof-of-concept, these SC-ISME probes have been demonstrated to record transient changes in extracellular K+ concentration in the cerebral cortex of living mice when the neurological phenomenon of spreading depression (SD) occurs, accompanied by changes in pH and O2. Furthermore, this versatile platform shows potential for combining different SC-ISMEs onto an individual probe to simultaneously in vivo monitor multiple ionic signals at different depths and locations in the brain of living rodents.
 Fig. 24  SC-ISME probes for in vivo physiological measurements. (a) An SC-ISME probe for the measurements of K+ in the living rodent brains at multiple depths and locations. (b) SEM image of the side view of the probe tip. (c) Photograph of the microelectrode tip. Reproduced with permission.555 Copyright 2015, Elsevier. (d) An SC-ISME probe for real-time monitoring of Ca2+ in the rat cortex during the SD process. (e) The occurrence of SD induced by local electrical stimulation leads to a decrease in extracellular Ca2+. (f) Photograph of the Ca2+-ISME. (g) SEM image of the Ca2+-ISME tip. Reproduced with permission.166 Copyright 2019, American Chemical Society. (h) Schematic diagram of a microneedle-shaped SC-ISME patch for intradermal K+ detection. (i) The results of the ex vivo verification test (inset: photograph of microneedle patch). (j) SEM image of the K+-ISME with a base thickness of 435 µm. (k) SEM image of the K+-ISM peeled off from the microneedle. Reproduced with permission.560 Copyright 2019, American Chemical Society. 
In other cases, He and coworkers fabricated SC-ISMEs by using a simple coated wire method for the determination of acetylcholine (Ach) in the rat brain homogenate.556 For the preparation of SC-ISMEs, PEDOT/PSS was coated on one end of the gold wire (0.5 mm diameter) as the solid-contact layer and then covered with a polymeric membrane cocktail containing heptakis(2,3,6-tri-O-methyl)-β-cyclodextrin as an Ach ionophore. These SC-ISMEs are stable over a temperature range of 15–40 °C and a pH range of 6.5–8.5 with a detection range of 10−5–10−1 M for Ach. The group of Mao developed SC-ISMEs for the real-time measurement of the dynamics of extracellular Ca2+ levels during the SD process in the brains of living rats (Fig. 24d–g).166 These Ca2+-ISMEs were constructed based on the CFEs (7 µm diameter) that were covered with the SHCN-based solid-contact layer and the membrane cocktail. Experiments show that these SC-ISMEs possess a good anti-biofouling ability and can maintain potential stability after 2 hours of implantation into the brain of live rats. Based on the CFE substrate, the same group also constructed H+-ISMEs,557 K+-ISMEs,246 and nanoporous CP-coated dopamine microelectrodes558 for the monitoring of physiological conditions of the living rat brains. Besides, they also discussed the construction of different SC-ISMEs for in vivo analysis in the field of brain neurochemistry.559
Apart from the measurements in the kidney or brain, the group of Crespo developed a potentiometric microneedle-shaped SC-ISME patch for intradermal ion detection (Fig. 24h–k).560 This analytical device consisting of a pair of microneedle-shaped SC-ISME and reference microelectrode was fixed in a polydimethylsiloxane (PDMS) epidermal patch and used for the detection of K+ levels in the subcutaneous interstitial fluid. For the construction of microneedle-like K+-ISMEs, functionalized MWCNTs were deposited on the top of the carbon-modified stainless-steel microneedle as the solid-contact layer. The obtained microneedle-like K+-ISMEs have a length of 1000 µm and a tip thickness of 15 µm. As a proof-of-concept, this microneedle patch exhibits no side effects on skin cells for at least 24 hours of in vitro cytotoxicity experiments and shows good reproducibility in animal skin insertion tests.
When considering the possible interactions and impacts between in vivo potentiometric biosensors and target objects, biocompatibility and biofouling are important factors that cannot be ignored.561,562 For these biomedical potentiometric ion sensing devices, especially for implantable and wearable measurements, the critical assessment of biocompatibility is necessary. Otherwise, undesirable host inflammatory reactions may be caused by using these unoptimized devices.563,564 Based on these considerations, the group of Crespo recommended that the biocompatibility assays should be done before further biomedical application of these potentiometric ion sensors configurated with the polymeric ISMs.565 They performed a series of in vitro cytotoxicity assessments of ISMs with different compositions, involving the assays of cell proliferation, viability, and adhesion with human dermal fibroblasts. The results reveal that valinomycin (K+ ionophore) and nonactin (NH4+ ionophore) leached from the ISM into the culture media are highly toxic to fibroblasts, thus greatly inhibiting cell proliferation. This inhibition phenomenon is even worse when the fibroblast monolayer is exposed to the ISMs containing the plasticizer (2-fluorophenyl 2-nitrophenylether, FNDPE) during cell adhesion tests. However, the use of mutacin as a potassium ionophore alternative for valinomycin shows no toxicity, suggesting its potential for the fabrication of biocompatible K+-ISEs.
On the other hand, enhanced biofouling resistance is also of significant importance to protect the sensor performance from the adverse impact of the surface accumulation of chemical or biological species (e.g., macromolecules and protein) on the sensing membrane.566,567 Such undesirable adsorption creates a barrier between the sensing area and the target analyte, leading to the increased noise signals and performance degradation of sensitivity, LOD, lifespan, etc. In this regard, the group of Lisak presented a method to study the kinetics of biofouling of SC-ISEs by using the combined technique of in situ potentiometry and null ellipsometry.57 The amount of bovine serum albumin (BSA) adsorbed on the surface of SC-ISEs and the accordingly resulting potential drift were quantitatively analyzed by this method. According to the test results, it is recommended to conduct the pre-equilibration of the sensor surface and sample solution before the actual clinical applications to avoid undesirable potential drops. Besides, the same group also researched the influence of phosphate buffer and BSA on the potentiometric response of SC-ISEs for heavy metal ion detection and found that the analytical performance at low analyte concentrations of SC-ISEs can be improved through the synergistic effect between the primary ion, conditioning solution, and surface-adsorbed biomolecule.568
For further enhancing the biocompatibility and anti-biofouling capability of these potentiometric ion sensors configurated with the ISM, several different strategies have been reported, such as changing the composition of the ISM, releasing active substances from the ISM, modifying the membrane surface by grafting biological or synthetic molecules, coating the ISM with a more biocompatible material, etc.569,570 Among them, the use of biocompatible material-based surface protective coatings is a relatively simple and versatile approach to improve biocompatibility and biofouling resistance,571 and different coating materials have been reported to achieve this goal, such as poly(ethylene glycol),572 heparin- modified chitosan,573 heparin modified bacterial cellulose,574 polydopamine,575 GO,576 SR,288 and so on. It is worth noting that the development and use of these enhancement strategies must be based on minimizing the impact on the response time, selectivity, and sensitivity of original sensors.577 Although these strategies have not yet been widely used for the development of SC-ISMEs, it is predicted that how to solve the issues of biocompatibility and biofouling will be one of the key factors to further improve the practicability of these in vivo SC-ISMEs.

4.2 Flexible SC-ISEs
The flexibility of ISEs comes from the improvement of conventional rigid electrodes, making them more suitable for flexible operating environments, especially for wearable concepts. Now, as one of the most attractive fields in the development of modern ISEs, considerable efforts have been devoted to improving their structure and performance for greater compatibility with wearable technologies. These flexible ISEs are integrated with wearable electronics as a part of the sensing component for the detection of ion activities in a variety of biofluids, which is also the main driving force for the development of flexible ISEs currently. The monitoring of certain ions in biofluids as the critical biomarkers can reflect a lot of information closely related to human physiological processes, which helps to better understand the electrolyte balance to maintain normal neural activities and basic metabolic functions. The employment of flexible ISEs in wearables offers an easy-to-use and cheap tool for quantitative analysis of in situ ion monitoring related to human health, allowing the detection of targeted analytes in a variety of biofluids. Taking the most common sweat analysis as an example, the broadly available ion selectivity of ISEs can cover major sweat analytes, such as Na+, K+, Ca+, NH4+, and Cl−, which are relatively abundant in sweat (∼mM level).578 In addition, integrated together with other sensors, such as electrochemical sensors (e.g., glucose) and physical sensors (e.g., temperature and strain),579 these wearable flexible electronics with potentiometric ion sensors can be connected to smart devices via Internet-of-Things (IoT) technology for real-time, continuous, comprehensive data acquisition of an individual's health and athletic performance.580 This stands as a promising alternative to conventional instrumental analytical techniques for the determination of human biomarkers using a simpler approach, showing unique attractiveness and great commercial potential.581,582
When looking back, in terms of in vivo monitoring extracellular ion activities in vascular endothelium and myocardium, attempts to prepare flexible ISEs have long been made to avoid undesirable damage to the electrode itself and the detected cells as a result of their rigidity and brittleness, such as the replacement of the glass body of micropipettes with plastic materials.477,583 But compared to the flexibility of modern planar microelectrodes, there is obviously two concepts.501,502 One of the first trials for obtaining a wearable sensor based on ISEs was reported by the group of Diamond in 2000.584 They used an array device of potentiometric ion microelectrodes as a small portable analytical instrument, which was connected to a wristwatch-like sweat sampler via a peristaltic pump, to simultaneously analyze Na+, K+, and Cl− in sweat samples with a portable PC. Ten years later, the same group reported the first example of wearable potentiometric ion sensing devices that can access real-time electrolyte data through a potentiometer during exercise.585 In recent years, benefiting from the advances in microelectronics, materials science, manufacturing methods, and chemical analysis techniques, flexible and stretchable bioelectronics have been applied for the development of SC-ISEs, which have further spearheaded the research development in potentiometric ion sensing devices for point-of-care diagnostic devices. These flexible ISEs with advanced design are integrated into a variety of wearables (such as wristbands, patches, tattoos, eyeglasses, clothing, etc.) to continuously detect a range of electrolyte indicators, characterized by their intimate and noninvasive integration with the soft curved surface of the human body.578,586 On the basis of previous statistics reported by Steinberg et al. in 2016, potentiometric ion sensors as frequently used analytical tools account for about a quarter of all wearable electrochemical sensors,587 and there is a reason to believe that this percentage is still increasing.
According to the reported literature, the solid-contact configuration of ISEs appears to be the only approach for wearable potentiometric ion sensing. Conventional liquid-contact ISEs are not compatible with modern flexible wearable technologies due to their inherent liquid compositions. Besides, any possible leakage of the inner filling solution will invalidate the sensor and also cause trouble to the wearer. In contrast, when it comes to wearable applications, the advantages of simple processing and reliability of SC-ISEs are more obvious and attractive, making them the current mainstream sensing tools. For these SC-ISEs exploited in the current flexible wearables, signal stability is of critical importance. In general, the development of wearable devices does not involve the exploration of new solid-contact functional materials. The selection of ion-to-electron transducers is usually based on the existing performance test reports and the compatibility of manufacturing technologies. Although the range of available ion–electron transducers is extensive, as to SC-ISEs integrated into wearable devices, CPs (e.g., PTDOT588–591) and carbon nanomaterials (e.g., CNTs,192,592–594 GR215,595,596) are particularly favored. A large number of studies and applications have proved the effective transduction function and good stability of PEDOT, making it the most commonly used CP for manufacturing wearable SC-ISEs.45 Another CP, PANI, is often used as the sensing layer of pH electrodes separately in wearables due to its intrinsic pH sensitivity.597–601 Carbon nanomaterials, as one of the favored transducer materials, can enhance the stability of the potentiometric signals due to their large double-layer capacitance. The employment of carbon nanomaterials allows the fabrication of flexible SC-ISEs without the need for conductive metal substrates. Using the customized functional inks based on carbon nanomaterials, patterned conductive electrodes can be generated on flexible and stretchable substrates using various printing techniques.602 In particular, carbon nanomaterials have more preparation strategies due to their unique properties. For example, high-performance GR-based electrodes can be directly prepared on different carbon-bearing substrates by simple one-step laser engraving, which has undoubtedly huge potential for the fabrication of flexible SC-ISEs.603,604
The development and application of flexible SC-ISEs incorporate the state-of-the-art manufacturing and analytical technologies. Nevertheless, when using these flexible SC-ISEs in wearable potentiometric ion sensing systems, there are still many limitations remaining to be addressed to better meet the requirements of the wearable concept. Apart from the basic requirements for measurement accuracy and reliability, these flexible SC-ISEs are necessary to be miniaturized to meet the requirement of finite sample volume and to possess acceptable wearing comfort, durability, lifespan, and biocompatibility. Another outstanding issue is the calibration of these sensors. Although SC-ISEs have made some progress in calibration-free measurements, they have not yet been expanded to wearable applications. Besides, when considering that target users are usually ordinary consumers rather than the experienced researchers, the operation of wearable devices must be user-friendly with easy-to-understand data readouts. Actual on-body measurements represent a complex application environment with various uncontrollable physical or chemical interference factors. The realization of a truly reliable wearable potentiometric ion sensing system requires not only robust flexible SC-ISEs, but also the optimization of the design of the entire galvanic cell, including the sample reservoirs and the REs that are often overlooked. In short, the wearable application of flexible SC-ISEs is both a challenge and an opportunity.8 The versatility and universality of wearable sensing platforms are of general reference significance for the development of portable devices, not only for on-body applications but also for environmental, agricultural, and industrial monitoring.

4.2.1 Fabrication technology. 
Flexible SC-ISEs are typically planar, miniaturized, and compatible with various flexible manufacturing technologies. Of these, apart from the common semiconductor manufacturing technologies for the fabrication of conductive metal electrodes, numerous technologies suitable for functional ink printing have also received extensive attention, allowing the simultaneous manufacturing of conductive electrodes and solid-contact layers. In addition, a variety of support materials and specific electrode designs endow these SC-ISEs with the desired characteristics, such as flexibility and stretchability. With the advances in fabrication technology and materials science, the production of flexible SC-ISEs is continuously developing toward achieving high throughput and low cost, promoting their further applications and commercialization.
Screen printing technology is a well-established approach for the production of a variety of electrochemical sensors605 and has also long been used for the development of SC-ISEs.34,502,606,607 As the most commonly used ink printing technology, screen printing is a stencil process using a mesh screen to transfer the functional ink onto the substrate, with the advantages of simplicity, low cost, and wide application scope.608,609 As shown in Fig. 25a, the group of Wang successfully used screen printing technology to prepare highly stretchable CNT-based electrodes, which can be used to construct flexible SC-ISEs.610 Benefitting from the intrinsic stretchability of the specially tailored CNT inks and elastomeric PU binders, as well as the synergistic design of serpentine structures, these CNT-based electrodes can maintain their structural integrity under an extremely large strain of up to 500%. For potentiometric ion sensing, these CNT-based electrodes were further functionalized with PU-based ISMs to realize flexible NH4+-ISEs, which display a stable potentiometric response during the entire mechanical resiliency test. Based on screen printing technology, the same group also constructed a series of flexible tattoo-based SC-ISEs.611,612 For example, Fig. 25b shows two types of wearable temporary transfer tattoo sensors for potentiometrically monitoring the pH and NH4+ level of sweat, respectively.613,614 In the fabrication process, conductive electrodes were first prepared via a thick-film screen printing manufacturing technique using a carbon fiber-doped ink and modified with functional sensing layers and then placed on the skin through the temporary transfer tattoo papers. The advantages of these tattoo-based SC-ISEs are that they are compliant with the skin and concealed in an artistic tattoo pattern and they can withstand repeated bending and stretching of the tattoos, while maintaining mechanical integrity and relatively stable analytical performance.
 Fig. 25  Flexible SC-ISEs fabricated with different technologies. (a) Screen-printing technology for the fabrication of a flexible and stretchable SC-ISE array. The CNT-based conductive electrodes are designed as a serpentine structure. Reproduced with permission.610 Copyright 2016, American Chemical Society. (b) Two kinds of cartoon or flower-like tattoo sensors fabricated by screen-printing technology. Reproduced with permission.613,614 Copyright 2013, Royal Society of Chemistry. (c) Flexible CNT-based SC-ISEs fabricated by transfer printing technology on the PI substrate (left) or temporary tattoo paper(right). Reproduced with permission.592 Copyright 2017, American Chemical Society. (d) Flexible GR-based SC-ISEs fabricated by spray coating technology on the paper substrate for sweat detection. Reproduced with permission.215 Copyright 2019, Elsevier. (e) R2R printing technology for the large-scale fabrication of flexible SC-ISEs on a 150 m PET web. Reproduced with permission.590 Copyright 2018, American Chemical Society. (f) Layer-by-layer microfluidic sensing architectures fabricated by R2R technology on a 100 m PET web. Reproduced with permission.49 Copyright 2019, The Authors. (g and h) Two kinds of flexible SC-ISE enabled sensing components fabricated using photolithography technology, with an iontophoresis module (g)589 or a temperature sensor (h).633 Reproduced with permission.589,633 Copyright 2017, National Academy of Sciences. Copyright 2016, American Chemical Society. (i) Flexible and stretchable porous cellular SC-ISE array network fabricated by photolithography technology, with the electrodeposited PEDOT/PSS-based solid-contact layer. Reproduced with permission.634 Copyright 2017, Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH & Co. KGaA, Weinheim. 
Transfer printing technology is a method to rapidly transfer patterns from a patterned template or mold to a receiving substrate, which is capable of heterogeneously integrating various electronic materials into the required flexible and stretchable substrates in a controllable manner.615 A key feature is that transfer printing technology overcomes the incompatibilities between the conventional fabrication protocols and unconventional substrates, allowing the separation of preparation and assembly processes of intricate electrical patterns and their eventual transfer onto the desired receiving substrates, which broadens the selection of substrates for the fabrication of flexible electronics and wearable sensors.616–619 For instance, Roy et al. developed flexible MWCNT-based SC-ISEs for wearable applications (Fig. 25c).592 Based on the transfer printing technique, MWCNTs grown on the SiO2/Si wafer substrates by a chemical vapor deposition (CVD) method can be transferred onto adhesive flexible substrates (e.g., temporary tattoo papers or Kapton tapes) to prepare flexible SC-ISE arrays. In particular, compared with gold, platinum, or screen-printed carbon electrodes, the ISM exhibits an enhanced attachment to MWCNT films due to the increased surface roughness. A wearable device containing MWCNT-based SC-ISEs and SC-REs was fabricated, which exhibited a response slope of 58 ± 3 mV per decade toward Na+ detection and can maintain stable operation for at least 1 hour.
Spray coating and inkjet printing, two droplet-based printing technologies, are also attractive for the preparation of flexible SC-ISEs due to their unique characteristics.620,621 Among them, spray coating technology is a relatively quick and simple preparation method, in which a diluted functional suspension is sprayed onto an inert supporting substrate using a pneumatic airbrush, usually accompanied by a heating process to evaporate the solvent for avoiding the aggregation caused by drying.360 With the help of spraying templates, patterned deposition can be easily achieved through spray coating. When using this technology to fabricate solid-contact layers and conductive substrates of SC-ISEs, selected functional inks are typically based on carbon nanomaterials, such as CNTs or GR suspensions in low-toxicity aqueous or organic solvents. For instance, the group of Niu demonstrated flexible SC-ISEs based on GR spray-coated hydrophobic paper for wearable applications (Fig. 25d).215 Specific shapes of electrode arrays were obtained through a corresponding mask. With four sensing channels, the integrated SC-ISE array is capable of simultaneously detecting pH, Cl−, Na+, and K+ in sweat. Because of the flow rate disturbance as a result of a small nozzle diameter or a low pressure, spray coating tends to produce scattered droplets, making the formation of very thin films with a high degree of uniformity difficult, which is sometimes considered a drawback of this technology.622 In this study, however, the wrinkled surface with high surface roughness of the spray-coated GR layer facilitates a tight connection to the ISM.
As for inkjet printing technology, it can realize digital high-precision multi-ink printing with controlled and adjustable processes and without the need for templates, which are widely used in prototype design or the small-scale production of flexible electronic devices.623–625 In recent years, several flexible SC-ISEs have been developed for routine analysis using this printing technology, such as inkjet-printed GR-based SC-ISEs,213 SC-ISEs constructed on inkjet-printed gold electrodes,626 and fully inkjet-printed paper-based SC-ISEs.216 In other cases, Shiwaku et al. used inkjet printing technology to develop an organic amplification system for wearable flexible SC-ISEs.78 However, compared to other technologies, the application of inkjet printing for the development of wearable flexible SC-ISEs is relatively scarce, which may be due to the limited range of printable inks and substrate materials and relatively high equipment costs. In addition, high-temperature processing and infrared sintering are often used to fabricate inkjet-printed electrodes, but are not preferred for flexible SC-ISEs based on a substrate that is not resistant to high temperature.627
For further reducing costs and for promoting commercialization, the large-scale, high-throughput, and uniform production of flexible SC-ISEs is essential. In this regard, roll-to-roll (R2R) printing technology, which relies on large rolls to measure and control the deposition of functional inks on the substrate surface, is a stronger viable candidate than other ink printing technologies.628 The group of Javery demonstrated the tremendous productivity of the R2R process, using which a mass of flexible carbon-based electrodes were fabricated on up to 150 m of a flexible substrate (Fig. 25e).590 These carbon-based electrodes can be further functionalized to develop disposable flexible SC-ISE test strips. Later, the same group introduced an approach to mass fabricate microfluidic sensing patches via R2R processes for sweat sensing (Fig. 25f).49 This wearable patch has two aligned layers, including a patterned sensing component layer for the fabricated flexible SC-ISEs and some other sensors to simultaneously monitor sweat biomarkers and rates, and a microfluidic adhesive layer with sweat collection reservoirs and spiral microfluidic channels to gather and guide sweat flow. However, on the other hand, the R2R printing technology is also characterized by high equipment and operation costs and the need for large quantities of printing inks. With the expectation of completing the prototype design of SC-ISEs using other complementary technologies and for further verifying their commercial viability, the large capital startup costs of the R2R technique can be averaged out when the production scale is large enough.625
In addition to ink printing technologies, the most used fabrication technology for the development of wearable flexible SC-ISEs based on metal electrode substrates is photolithography.629–632Fig. 25g and h show two typical wearable sensing modules fabricated using photolithography technology, in which flexible SC-ISEs are combined with iontophoresis electrodes and temperature sensors, respectively.589,633 With the use of a programmable iontophoresis electrode, a wearable flexible SC-ISE-based platform can promote periodic sweat extraction from sedentary individuals for in situ physiological analysis.589 The combination of flexible SC-ISEs and temperature sensors enables the real-time continuous analysis of body fluids and skin temperature for disease diagnosis.633Fig. 25i illustrates a flexible and stretchable SC-ISE array with a precise open cellular substrate to facilitate solution exchange for use in bio-integrated electronic devices.634 A flexible SC-ISE array with eight sites is mounted on a stretchable PDMS cellular substrate, in which the interconnecting wires possess a lithographically defined serpentine structure to achieve biaxial stretchability. Three types of SC-ISEs were constructed based on the PEDOT/PSS-enabled solid-contact layer and ionophore-doped polymeric membrane for the detection of H+, K+, and Ca2+, respectively. Within the biologically relevant range of ion concentrations, these SC-ISEs exhibit comparable analytical performance to previously reported counterparts constructed on non-stretchable substrates and can remain stable for up to 2 days of continuous immersion in water. In general, photolithography allows the high-resolution manufacture of conductive patterns for specific design requirements; however, the relative complexity of the manufacturing process based on this technology may be a limiting factor for its large-scale application in the development of flexible SC-ISEs.
The flexibility of SC-ISEs has its roots in the intrinsic characteristics of functional materials and substrate materials.635,636 Typical substrate materials for the development of flexible SC-ISEs are inert polymer materials, such as PET588–590,633,637 and PDMS.595,596,634 PET-based substrates possess excellent mechanical bendability, durability, and high transparency, but are not stretchable.638 PDMS is the most commonly used stretchable substrate material, characterized by simple processing, stable chemical properties, and non-toxicity.639 Elastomeric PDMS substrates can be incorporated with stretchable functional materials and electrode structures or mixed with other electronic materials for increased stretch recovery.640,641 Another common commercially available polymer, PI, has excellent thermal and chemical resistance and insulating features, and thus it has been extensively used as a flexible substrate for electronic circuits.642,643 However, PI is not highly transparent and cannot withstand large tensile stresses. Its intrinsic color and unstretchability limit its application in wearable sensing modules.644
Apart from synthetic polymers, considerable efforts have also been made to try other ordinary materials as supporting substrates for wearable flexible SC-ISEs, such as temporary transfer tattoo papers,612 carbon adhesive tapes,645 carbon fibers,646 cotton yarns,192 threads,647 and textiles.648,649 Taking textiles as an example, flexible textile-based SC-ISEs can be integrated into smart clothing, relying on the rich elastomeric properties of textiles to achieve conformal contact between the device and the human body for real-time analysis. The group of Wang reported a flexible and stretchable textile-based SC-ISE array (Fig. 26a).594 A screen-printed MWCNT-based serpentine conductive pattern was directly mounted on different fabric materials functionalized with PU-based ISMs to simultaneously monitor K+ and Na+ in sweat. Fig. 26b shows another different strategy for the preparation of SC-ISEs from textiles.591 In this study, flexible SC-ISEs were constructed on electrode substrates based on highly conductive nitrogen-doped carbon textiles annealed from silk fabrics. This integrated platform can be used to simultaneously detect multiplex biomarkers, including K+ and Na+. The flexibility of the whole system was also demonstrated through the fabrication of the sensing patch on a common silk fabric.
 Fig. 26  (a) Flexible textile-based SC-ISE array for the determination of Na+ and K+ in sweat. Reproduced with permission.594 Copyright 2016, Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH & Co. KGaA, Weinheim. (b) Flexible SC-ISE enabled multiplex electrochemical sensor array with silk fabric derivative-based conductive electrodes. Reproduced with permission.591 Copyright 2019, the authors. 


4.2.2 Flexible SC-ISE-enabled wearable devices. 
Wireless wearable ion sensing systems. 
Wearable ion sensing is the most important application of flexible SC-ISEs. A typical wireless wearable ion sensing system consists of two parts, including a sensing component for signal transduction and an electronic component for signal conditioning, processing, and transmission.578 In general, flexible SC-ISEs are integrated with other physical or chemical sensors to form the sensing component, while the precision-designed electronic component is the key to realizing the sensing function. The configuration strategies of these electronic components are generally based on the combination of traditional silicon microchips and flexible substrates, including flexible PCBs and soft polymers printed with conductive elements.595,596,650–652 When considering the options of various wireless and contactless approaches, smartphone-compatible technologies have a unique appeal in the development of wireless wearable ion sensing systems. For a better understanding of the design, manufacture, and operation of these systems, here is an excellent example presented by Gao et al., who developed an integrated wireless wearable platform that can be packaged as a smart wristband or headband (Fig. 27a).588 Flexible Na+- and K+-ISEs were integrated with glucose, lactate, and temperature sensors to realize the multiplexed sensing of informative biomarkers in sweat. The integrated circuit component was fabricated on a flexible PCB, consisting of analog circuits for the implementation of signal-conditioning paths, a pre-programmed microcontroller with a built-in analog-to-digital converter block to calibrate the conditioned signals, and a Bluetooth transceiver for data transmission to a custom-developed mobile application. As to a Bluetooth-based device, the Bluetooth module in the electronic component dominates its power consumption, which determines how long it can operate. Although the reduced overall power consumption can be achieved through the use of Bluetooth Low Energy (BLE) technology,653 these BLE-based devices still require relatively large, bulky hardware and power batteries to realize advanced wireless communication, limiting their further miniaturization.
 Fig. 27  (a) An integrated Bluetooth-based wearable sensor array packaged as a smart wristband or headband for multiplexed perspiration analysis. Reproduced with permission.588 Copyright 2016, Springer Nature. (b) A smartphone enabled NFC-based battery-free wearable multisensor device for sweat analysis. Reproduced with permission.596 Copyright 2019, Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH & Co. KGaA, Weinheim. (c) An eyeglass-based wireless device with a nose pad sensing component for real-time monitoring of electrolytes and metabolites in sweat. Reproduced with permission.681 Copyright 2017, Royal Society of Chemistry. (d) Flexible printed SC-ISEs on a variety of common textiles for sweat analysis. Reproduced with permission.594 Copyright 2016, Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH & Co. KGaA, Weinheim. (e) A soft intraoral monitoring device for real-time quantifying Na+ intake. Reproduced with permission.680 Copyright 2018, National Academy of Sciences. (f) A multiplexed epidermal patch with a porous sponge to absorb sweat. Reproduced with permission.596 Copyright 2019, Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH & Co. KGaA, Weinheim. (g) A band-aid style sweat patch with an absorbing paper pad to absorb sweat. Reproduced with permission.652 Copyright 2015, IEEE. (h) A sweatband fluidic platform with an open-structured sampling channel to gather sweat. Reproduced with permission.229 Copyright 2017, American Chemical Society. (i) A flexible epidermal patch with a serpentine microfluidic channel for sweat capture and flow. Reproduced with permission.695 Copyright 2019, Royal Society of Chemistry. 
To circumvent these tradeoffs, near-field communication (NFC) has been used as an attractive wireless communication alternative to Bluetooth to design smaller, lighter, more flexible electronic components for SC-ISE-enabled wearable devices.654–657 Based on the inductive coupling principle, NFC technology is compatible with both high-efficiency power transfer and wireless data transmission.658,659 An attractive key is that NFC-based wearables allow passive energy reception from the receiving device to achieve battery-free device architectures with a relatively small component count.595,652 For instance, Xu et al. demonstrated a battery-free wireless epidermal electrochemical system with an NFC communication module, which enabled both wireless powering and communication (Fig. 27b).596 The sensing component of this device was composed of three types of flexible SC-ISEs and a glucose sensor for the simultaneous detection of H+, K+, Na+, and glucose levels in sweat. As to the matching flexible circuit, it was fitted with an analog front end (AFE), a microcontroller unit (MCU), and an NFC chip, exploiting a multilayer design, including the PI substrate layer and PDMS encapsulation layer, to minimize bending-induced strains. The NFC-enabled smartphones can connect wirelessly to this wearable device via inductive coupling with the NFC antennas. A custom mobile application with a user-friendly interface was developed to display analysis data from the sensors in real time. Nevertheless, due to the near-field properties of this technology, even if these receiving devices have high transmission power, NFC-based wearables can only achieve shorter-range interactions with them. On the other hand, the limited transmitter–receiver distance is thought to guarantee the security of data transmission and enhance anti-interference, and in some cases allows users to readily control the continuous and autonomous sensing.578 Therefore, prior to implementation, the characteristics of the distance and sampling frequency between NFC-based wearables and NFC-enabled devices should be fully understood.
At present, as two main wireless communication protocols, Bluetooth and NFC technologies have been widely used for the development of various SC-ISE-enabled wireless wearable devices.587 These two technologies have their respective advantages and constraints; however, from the perspective of high-density wireless data communication, in which multiple SC-ISE-enabled wearable devices require high-rate interactions, neither of these technologies are suitable for amplified connectivity requirements.580 Other options, including high-frequency (HF) and ultrahigh-frequency (UHF) technologies, are much more limited in epidermal wearables and therefore less practical currently.635 Apart from the need for a reasonable choice of wireless communication protocols, simplifying components, reducing power consumption, and exploring new energy supplies are also important for development of new-generation SC-ISE-enabled wireless wearable devices. For instance, many efforts have been made to find new alternatives to conventional batteries, such as nanogenerators,660–664 solar cells,665–667 biofuel cells,668–670 and micro-supercapacitors,671–674 to achieve high energy harvesting and storage capabilities for smart wearable electronics. Based on these novel technologies and strategies, development of more flexible and durable SC-ISE-enabled smart wireless wearable devices is expected.
The types of SC-ISE-enabled wearable devices. 
The use of wireless and contactless technologies enables SC-ISE-based wearable devices to have practical feasibilities for continuous, non-invasive, and real-time monitoring of an individual's health status and exercise performance using a comfortable method, without compromising the welfare of the wearer. Based on the Bluetooth or NFC wireless communication protocol, a variety of wearables with flexible SC-ISEs have been developed for different parts of the body, including watches,675,676 wristbands,588,589,591,677 epidermal patches,595,596,652,678,679 tattoos,611 intraoral electronics,680 eyeglass,681 textiles,594etc. From the perspective of design strategies, these devices can be roughly divided into two categories, one is the combination of sensing components and necessary wearables of individuals (e.g., eyeglass and textiles) and the other is specially designed functional wearable devices (e.g., epidermal patches and intraoral electronics).
Integrating wearable ion sensing devices into individual essential wearables can measure human physiological indicators without the need for additional wearable devices. The group of Wang presented a wireless integrated eyeglass sensing system capable of real-time detecting K+ and lactate in sweat (Fig. 27c).681 The sensing components were cleverly positioned on two nose-bridge pads, including a K+-ISE and a lactate biosensor that are connected with a wireless electronic module on the arm of the spectacle. This eyeglass system provides a compatible sensing platform with interchangeable-sensing features, allowing the replacement of nose-bridge sensor stickers to detect different sweat electrolytes and metabolites. In another example, flexible SC-ISEs were fabricated on different common textiles for the detection of electrolyte levels in sweat (Fig. 27d).594 The combination of sensors and textiles shows some advantages, such as comfort and washability. Moreover, due to the intrinsic elasticity of the textiles and the stretchability of custom inks and conductive patterns, such textile-based wearable potentiometric ion sensing systems can withstand large stretching and bending deformations. From the development perspective, the integration of textile-based SC-ISEs and portable wireless data transmission devices makes it possible for a common garment to become a smart sweat monitoring platform.
As to specially designed functional wearable devices, here is a special example of a soft intraoral monitoring device that has been designed to real-time quantify Na+ intake through a remote wireless telemetry method (Fig. 27e).680 This intraoral sensing system integrates miniaturized SC-ISEs and ultrathin stretchable electronic components that enable comfortable contact with intraoral tissue. The demonstration of real-time recording of Na+ levels in the saliva of healthy subjects proved the feasibility of this device to monitor Na+ intake for hypertension management. Nevertheless, compared to SC-ISE-enabled epidermal wearable devices, the complex oral environment (including the adverse effects of saliva components and food residues) puts forward higher design requirements on these types of intraoral wearables.
Sampling method. 
For the practical applications of these wireless wearables containing flexible SC-ISEs, an important factor that cannot be ignored is how to obtain enough biofluid sample volumes. Although the miniaturized ISEs have been proved to have the ability to detect trace ion levels in confined samples,476,548 the premise of potentiometric ion sensing is that even if there is only a low sample volume, a well-defined galvanic cell must be formed between the WE and RE, as well as the sample solution. In routine analysis, the use of auxiliary sampling modules (e.g., paper and sponge) is a common and effective method for collecting or separating target analytes from small liquid samples.682–686 For sampling methods in wearable applications, taking the most common sweat sensing as an example, several similar strategies have also been adopted to tackle this problem, involving wicking pads, sampling cells, and microfluidics. Of these, wicking pads made of various sweat-absorbing materials are widely used as sweat-uptake layers to gather sweat due to their simplicity and effectiveness.588,589,679,687 These pads cover the surface of the sensing components and connect with the human skin to absorb sweat through capillary force. Fig. 27f and g show two types of wicking pads made of porous cellulose sponge and absorbing paper, respectively.596,652 Nevertheless, the sensing components with these structures cannot distinguish between new and older sweat, and thus they are usually disposable, or require frequent replacement of the wicking pads to recycle the sensors.688,689 In another instance, SC-ISE-enabled wearable devices with sampling cells can continuously accumulate fresh sweat through a large open structure (Fig. 27h).229 However, in this case, sweat collection requires the wearer to have a high sweat rate via a certain level of exercise or an external stimulus, which is not universally applicable.
When more complex actual conditions are considered, e.g., irregular sweating, low sweat rates, sweat renewal, and the possibility of evaporation and contamination, well-designed wearable microfluidic devices show their unique appeal.604,690–693 The group of Diamond developed several polymethyl methacrylate (PMMA)-based microfluidic chips incorporating highly absorbent cotton threads to assist passive fluid transport for sensing Na+ levels in sweat.675–677 However, the rigid nature of the PMMA material is not conducive to establishing close contact with the skin and may cause discomfort to the wearer. In pursuit of flexibility and stretchability, most microfluidic substrates are based on PDMS. The group of Wang presented an integrated epidermal microfluidic potentiometric device containing a soft PDMS-based microfluidic patch.678 The microfluidic network has four inlet channels to provide a sufficient amount of sweat and one outlet channel to ensure that the generated sweat efficiently flowed through the centered SC-ISEs to detect Na+ and K+ levels. The group of Javey fabricated a wearable microfluidic sensing patch with a spiral-patterned microfluidic channel that can spontaneously pump the secreted sweat to enable sweat ion analysis with the use of SC-ISEs.694 Later, the same group also reported a flexible multi-model epidermal sensing patch with a serpentine microfluidic channel for non-invasive biofluid and electrolyte secretion analysis (Fig. 27i).695 During the analysis, sweat flows sequentially through the integrated sensors (an Na+-ISE, an impedimetric sensor, and a sweat rate sensor) along the channel, enabling this microfluidic device to simultaneously monitor Na+ levels, total ionic charge concentration, and the sweat rate. In general, well-designed encapsulated chambers and controlled channels of microfluidics enable sweat flow within the restricted domain with the decoupling of its production and sensing, thereby facilitating accurate sweat analysis. With this configuration, wearable devices cannot only avoid undesirable evaporation and contamination of sweat samples but also reduce the mixing and carry-over effects.

5. Summary and outlook
For nearly half a century since their inception, SC-ISEs, as a new generation of potentiometric ion sensors, have exhibited unique attractiveness and have become one of the indispensable essential tools for ion analysis in a great variety of applications. Here, following an overview of the basic concept of SC-ISEs, we have presented a comprehensive review of recent advances in solid-contact functional materials, with an emphasis on the miniaturization and flexibility of SC-ISEs. Given the rapid pace of development in this field, what we provide herein may be only a momentary view. Nevertheless, we hope the issues discussed in this article can provide some new perspectives and useful guidance for the development of SC-ISEs and inspire more exciting innovations and applications in this expanding field of potentiometric ion sensors.
The emergence of ion-to-electron transducers for SC-ISEs marks a milestone in the development of modern potentiometric ion sensors with significant improvements in response stability and reproducibility. To date, a number of functional materials have been proved to be effective ion-to-electron transducers for SC-ISEs by acting as asymmetric capacitors with redox capacitance or double-layer capacitance. However, due to a variety of properties and preparation methods of these functional materials, it is almost impossible to determine which one is the most suitable to serve as the solid-contact layer. In addition, differences in experimental approaches may also result in disparate interpretations of even the same functional material. In other words, there is still a lack of a universally accepted solid-contact layer platform for the preparation of SC-ISEs with different ISMs. In this context, the standard test protocols and common evaluation criteria need to be further refined to more fully standardize the development of SC-ISEs and provide clear and comparable parameters between different solid-contact functional materials. Besides, in view of the extensive selection of the existing functional materials, the method of demonstrating the improved performance characteristics of newly developed SC-ISEs by comparison with CWEs should be extended to other excellent choices, such as the use of control groups based on CPs, carbon nanomaterials, etc. In the years to come, it is certain that the pursuit of solid-contact functional materials that are more in line with ideal requirements and more versatile will still be an important focus for the development of robust SC-ISEs.
Based on the continuous innovation and advancement of theory, materials, technology, and design, considerable efforts have been made to improve the sensitivity, selectivity, LOD, lifespan, biocompatibility, and anti-biofouling capability of SC-ISEs, as well as to extend their detection capabilities beyond common ions. The miniaturized and flexible versions of SC-ISEs have also been widely used, which has further broadened the application fields of SC-ISEs, such as in vivo biomedical measurements and wearable point-of-care analysis. Meanwhile, by combining with advanced electronic components, SC-ISE-enabled devices have been able to perform remote ion detection wirelessly with more intelligent data acquisition and analysis capabilities. Besides, the use of dynamic electrochemistry protocols has transformed the sensing concepts of SC-ISEs from conventional zero-current potentiometry to dynamic potentiometry with more readout approaches. Nevertheless, despite these considerable advancements, many aspects of SC-ISEs still need to be further developed to enable large-scale manufacturing and applications towards commercialization. In order to meet these requirements, aside from the exploration of more ideal solid-contact functional materials, the demand for new membrane materials and ionophores and further optimization of the fabrication and equilibration conditions are equally urgent. In addition, although SC-ISEs have made significant development in terms of calibration-free and maintenance-free measurements, they are still in the infancy stage when considering practical applications. In short, there are co-existing opportunities and challenges in the current development of SC-ISEs. Thanks to the continuous progress made by numerous research groups around the world, it is believed that there will be more fundamental and technological breakthroughs in this field, with grander application prospects.

Yuzhou Shao
	Yuzhou Shao received his BS (2018) degree from the School of Biosystems Engineering and Food Science at Zhejiang University. He is currently studying for his MS degree under the supervision of Prof. Jianfeng Ping. His current research focuses on nanomaterial-based battery-free wireless biosensing devices for agriculture.

Yibin Ying
	Yibin Ying received his PhD degree in agricultural engineering. Now he is a Qiushi Distinguished Professor of Zhejiang University and the President of Zhejiang A&F University. He leads the Intelligent Bioindustrial Equipment Innovation Team at Zhejiang University. His research interests focus on the development of technology and intelligent equipment for agricultural products.

Jianfeng Ping
	Jianfeng Ping is a ZJU-100 Young Professor at Zhejiang University. He obtained his BS degree from the Zhejiang University of Technology and his PhD degree from Zhejiang University. His current research interests focus on battery-free, flexible, stretchable, wireless, green, biodegradable, breathable, and wearable sensing devices for agriculture.

 	Fig. 5  (a) Theoretical potential response curve of the SC-ISEs in the presence of a thin water layer (red line) or in the absence of a thin layer water (blue line) during the water layer test. (b) Schematic illustration of the test for the presence of a water layer based on the transmembrane diffusion of CO2. When a water layer forms at the backside of the H+-ISM, the corresponding changes in the pH value caused by the increase of CO2 concentration in the sample solution will result in a significant negative potential drift.
